post</a>.</p>","descriptionType":"text/html","publishedDate":"Mon, 05 Apr 2021 18:24:00 +0000","feedId":70,"bgimg":"https://4.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS590x0~articles/5433360964/0246E711-97F1-4989-86D2-28D0C7478E7A.jpeg","linkMd5":"b4a346291520cafb673e6a8a2c684bf3","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx29/cdn57@2020_5/2021/04/07/17-38-14-514_bb2d101d7e413bc8.webp","destWidth":590,"destHeight":442,"sourceBytes":32516,"destBytes":12866,"author":"","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://4.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS590x0~articles/5433360964/0246E711-97F1-4989-86D2-28D0C7478E7A.jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx29/cdn57@2020_5/2021/04/07/17-38-14-514_bb2d101d7e413bc8.webp","https://2.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS590x0~articles/5433360964/EB4139B6-F356-4F6F-B570-B53F4B9AE663.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn12@2020_5/2021/04/07/17-38-31-984_a277e5ae7726716c.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1617817093462},{"createdTime":"2021-04-08 01:38:13","updatedTime":"2021-04-08 01:38:13","title":"If you shoot Log on the Canon EOS R5, you should shoot C-Log3. Here's why.","link":"https://www.dpreview.com/articles/3873565570/when-you-shoot-log-on-the-canon-eos-r5-shoot-c-log3-here-s-why","description":"<table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCrop singleNoBorder center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"590\"> \n <tbody> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 590px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/3873565570/Canon_EOS_R5.jpeg\" target=\"article-3873565570\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"590\" height=\"393\" src=\"https://2.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS590x0~articles/3873565570/Canon_EOS_R5.jpeg\" width=\"590\" data-filename=\"Canon_EOS_R5.jpeg\" /></a></td> \n  </tr> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"caption\" style=\"width: 590px;\">From somewhat inauspicious beginnings, firmware updates are turning the EOS R5 into an increasingly capable video camera</td> \n  </tr> \n </tbody> \n</table> \n<p>With its latest firmware, the Canon EOS R5 gains the Canon Log 3 profile for video. In this article, we're taking a closer look at C-Log3 and how it differs from the existing C-Log profile. In doing so, we hope to make clear why cameras sometimes offer multiple Log profiles, to help you decide which one to use.</p> \n<h3>Why Log?</h3> \n<p>To understand why cameras have different Log profiles, it's worth going back to basics to explain why videographers shoot Log at all.</p> \n<p>In stills photography we generally choose between JPEG files (a small and efficient compressed format but one that has limited editing flexibility), and Raw files (larger but retaining the greatest flexibility). Log is an attempt at a middle ground between these two: it's subject to a lot of the processing and compression that a JPEG file is, but has been expressly designed to retain enough information about the original capture to remain flexible. Crucially, it tends to be relatively small, which is valuable in video: when you're measuring file sizes in data per second, then the clock is ticking from the moment you hit the [REC] button.</p> \n<p>The simplest way to think of Log files is like JPEGs but with tone curves designed to share their data values out more equally between the number of stops you captured. Colors are also desaturated, to reduce the risk of saturated parts of the scene clipping and hence losing flexibility when color grading.</p> \n<h3>Why are there different versions of Log?</h3> \n<p>In the previous section I wrote that Log curves are designed to retain similar amounts of information about every stop of light you captured. This isn't quite correct. More precisely, Log curves are designed to encode a pre-determined number of stops of light. And there are a number of reasons why more is not always better.</p> \n<p>Firstly, there's simply no point using a Log curve that encodes 15 stops of light if you sensor can only capture 12 before the signal becomes indistinguishable from noise. For a start, it would mean that the bottom three stops of your file would be a noisy mess, but it would also encourage you to use an inappropriate exposure.</p> \n<table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCrop singleNoBorder center\" data-image-height=\"\" data-image-width=\"590\"> \n <tbody> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 590px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/3873565570/C_Log_graph.png\" target=\"article-3873565570\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"1180\" height=\"404\" src=\"https://3.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS1180x0~articles/3873565570/C_Log_graph.png\" width=\"590\" data-filename=\"C_Log_graph.png\" /></a></td> \n  </tr> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"caption\" style=\"width: 590px;\">C-Log is designed to accommodate around 11 stops of DR. In order to capture around 2EV more highlights than a standard JPEG, it's supposed to be exposed as ISO 400 (rather than the ISO 100 that's the base setting for the Standard color mode). Canon Log 3's base ISO setting is rated as 800, to capture an additional stop.</td> \n  </tr> \n </tbody> \n</table> \n<p>If we assume the Log curve is designed to incorporate another two stops of highlights over what a standard sRGB JPEG would include, you'd need to reduce exposure by two stops to capture this additional highlight information. A two-stop reduction in exposure means a two-stop increase in noise in all those tones that overlap with the standard color mode.</p> \n<p>The final consideration is data availability. Your camera can only record a certain number of brightness values. If you try to share those values roughly equally between 11 stops of light, you retain more information about each one than if you try to squeeze 15 stops into the file. This is less of a problem on higher-end cameras that shoot 10-bit footage (and so have 1024 values to share), but is worth considering if your camera only captures 8-bit Log, and hence has only 256 values available.</p> \n<p>This should start to explain why there are multiple Log options: you want to find a Log curve that's well suited both to the capabilities of your camera and to the scene you're shooting.</p> \n<h3>C-Log vs C-Log3</h3> \n<p>We took a closer look at the Canon Log and Canon Log 3 curves and what difference they make. The first thing you may notice upon engaging C-Log3 is that the base ISO rating jumps to 800: one stop higher than the existing C-Log mode. We've checked, and there's no change in amplification: that one stop change in ISO rating is solely an instruction to give the camera one stop less exposure, to capture more highlights.</p> \n<div class=\"contentTable\"> \n <table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"contentTable\"> \n  <tbody> \n   <tr> \n    <th width=\"33.333333333333336%\">Mode</th> \n    <th width=\"33.333333333333336%\">Base ISO rating</th> \n    <th width=\"33.333333333333336%\">Difference from sRGB<span class=\"green\">*</span></th> \n   </tr> \n   <tr> \n    <th width=\"33.333333333333336%\">Standard (sRGB)</th> \n    <td width=\"33.333333333333336%\">100</td> \n    <td width=\"33.333333333333336%\">0</td> \n   </tr> \n   <tr> \n    <th width=\"33.333333333333336%\">Canon Log</th> \n    <td width=\"33.333333333333336%\">400</td> \n    <td width=\"33.333333333333336%\">+2EV</td> \n   </tr> \n   <tr> \n    <th width=\"33.333333333333336%\">Canon Log 3</th> \n    <td width=\"33.333333333333336%\">800</td> \n    <td width=\"33.333333333333336%\">+3EV</td> \n   </tr> \n  </tbody> \n </table> \n</div> \n<p>Here are the waveforms of C-Log and C-Log3, exposed with this change in ISO rating taken into account. As theory leads us to expect, this results in an extra stop of highlight capture but with a noise increase (the waveforms of each step becoming taller/fuzzier), for the rest of the tones.</p> \n<table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCrop\" data-image-height=\"\" data-image-width=\"590\"> \n <tbody> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"image\" colspan=\"2\" style=\"width: 576px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/3873565570/CLog-1_exp.png\" target=\"article-3873565570\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"1152\" height=\"435\" id=\"WF2\" src=\"https://2.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS1152x0~articles/3873565570/CLog-1_exp.png\" width=\"576\" data-filename=\"CLog-1_exp.png\" /></a></td> \n  </tr> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"caption imageSwapper active\" style=\"width: 50%;\" data-image-id=\"WF2\" data-image-src=\"https://1.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS1152x0~articles/3873565570/CLog-1_exp.png?v=5287\" data-large-image-src=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/3873565570/CLog-1_exp.png\"> <p class=\"newsLink\">C-Log</p> </td> \n   <td class=\"caption imageSwapper\" style=\"width: 50%;\" data-image-id=\"WF2\" data-image-src=\"https://1.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS1152x0~articles/3873565570/CLog-3.png?v=5287\" data-large-image-src=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/3873565570/CLog-3.png\"> <p class=\"newsLink\">C-Log3</p> </td> \n  </tr> \n </tbody> \n</table> \n<p>Of course you don't have to expose this way, if you'd prefer not to. The inherent flexibility of Log means you could expose C-Log3 as if it were C-Log, clip highlights at the same point and gain your extra stop in the shadows, instead.</p> \n<table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCrop\" data-image-height=\"\" data-image-width=\"590\"> \n <tbody> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"image\" colspan=\"2\" style=\"width: 576px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/3873565570/CLog-1.png\" target=\"article-3873565570\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"1152\" height=\"435\" id=\"WF\" src=\"https://4.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS1152x0~articles/3873565570/CLog-1.png\" width=\"576\" data-filename=\"CLog-1.png\" /></a></td> \n  </tr> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"caption imageSwapper active\" style=\"width: 50%;\" data-image-id=\"WF\" data-image-src=\"https://3.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS1152x0~articles/3873565570/CLog-1.png?v=5287\" data-large-image-src=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/3873565570/CLog-1.png\"> <p class=\"newsLink\">C-Log</p> </td> \n   <td class=\"caption imageSwapper\" style=\"width: 50%;\" data-image-id=\"WF\" data-image-src=\"https://1.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS1152x0~articles/3873565570/CLog-3.png?v=5287\" data-large-image-src=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/3873565570/CLog-3.png\"> <p class=\"newsLink\">C-Log3 (matched exposure)</p> </td> \n  </tr> \n </tbody> \n</table> \n<p>But the difference between the two profiles isn't just a question of C-Log3 being slightly flatter, to incorporate an extra stop of DR. Look closely at the noise floor, represented by the thick white band at the bottom of the waveform. At first glance, this appears taller (noisier) for C-Log3. But this shouldn't be the case, since we gave identical exposure to both modes.</p> \n<p>Look closer and you'll see that the noise in C-Log3 mode extends the same distance above and below the 128 marker line, which is what you'd expect: noise is variation above and below the 'true' value. But in C-Log mode, it extends upwards by the same amount as C-Log3, but cuts off cleanly just below a value of 128. Canon is using a very high black clipping level to make the darkest tones appear less noisy.</p> \n<p>The impact of this can sometimes reveal itself when you try to grade the footage: C-Log will sometimes plug-up blacks, which look unnatural if they're brightened during color grading. C-Log3 doesn't clip its blacks so aggressively, so there's less risk of the darker tones looking strange when lifted.</p> \n<div class=\"beer-slider-container\">\n <div id=\"slider2\" class=\"beer-slider\" data-beer-label=\"C-Log3 (Cine)\">\n  <img src=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS1180x0~articles/3873565570/Jordan_CL3_LUT.jpeg\">\n   <div class=\"beer-reveal\" data-beer-label=\"C-Log (EOS)\">\n    <img src=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS1180x0~articles/3873565570/Jordan_CL1_LUT.jpeg\" />\n   </div></img>\n </div>\n</div> \n<div class=\"caption\">\n It's also worth noting that C-Log3 gives you a choice of Cine or Rec 709 color response (rather than the EOS or Neutral options for Canon Log), making it compatible with the LUTs Canon has created for its Cinema EOS cameras, and giving a more interesting starting point.\n</div> \n<p>So C-Log3's greater processing flexibility comes from more than just the additional stop its tone curve is designed to provide. However, given how noisy the shadows get, it should be pretty clear that it's already pushing at the limits of what the EOS R5 is able to capture.</p> \n<p>This makes sense: the R5 creates its video from a 12-bit sensor readout. And, although the process of downscaling from 8K to 4K will boost the number a bit, it's never going to significantly exceed 12 stops of DR capture. As such, the C-Log3 curve seems a pretty good match for the camera, and it's unlikely that Canon will add the even wider DR C-Log2 profile.</p> \n<h3>When should I use it?</h3> \n<p>Canon Log 3 offers a little more dynamic range than Canon Log, but it's also less prone to clogged-up shadows and is more readily compatible with the LUTs designed for Canon's Cinema EOS cameras. Both of these factors make it more useable than the existing C-Log profile.</p> \n<p>If you're worried about the additional noise and don't need the additional stop of dynamic range, there's no reason you can't overexpose C-Log3 by a stop and pretend you're still shooting with a slightly more sophisticated version of C-Log. The wider DR captured does seem to slightly increase the risk of posterization, though.</p> \n<div class=\"beer-slider-container\">\n <div id=\"slider1\" class=\"beer-slider\" data-beer-label=\"C-Log3 (matched exposure)\">\n  <img src=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS1180x0~articles/3873565570/Scene_CL3_LUT.jpeg\">\n   <div class=\"beer-reveal\" data-beer-label=\"C-Log\">\n    <img src=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS1180x0~articles/3873565570/Scene_CL1_LUT.jpeg\" />\n   </div></img>\n </div>\n</div> \n<div class=\"caption\">\n This scene was given the same exposure (ignoring the different ISO ratings) and with curves adjustment applied to the C-Log3 footage before the LUT was applied to give a matched starting point. Another curve, lifting the shadows was the applied to both images, to show the effect of brightening the shadows. \n <br><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/3873565570/Scene_CL1_LUT.jpeg\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">Click here to download the C-Log image</a><br><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/3873565570/Scene_CL3_LUT.jpeg\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">Click here to download the C-Log3 version</a></br></br>\n</div> \n<p>Of course this doesn't mean it suddenly makes sense to shoot Log all the time: the reduced, highlight capturing exposures mean it may not be ideal in low light, and it may be unnecessary or ill-suited to low contrast or controlled lighting shoots. But when it makes sense to shoot log on the R5, we think it makes sense to choose C-Log3.</p> \n<hr> \n <p><span class=\"green\">*The increase in base ISO rating will correspond to the number of additional stops of highlights the Log curve is designed to accommodate. This isn't always the case (some cameras also add a little amplification to improve shadow noise), but in our tests of the R5, we're seeing no amplification change between modes.</span></p>\n</hr>","descriptionType":"text/html","publishedDate":"Wed, 07 Apr 2021 14:00:00 +0000","feedId":70,"bgimg":"https://2.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS590x0~articles/3873565570/Canon_EOS_R5.jpeg","linkMd5":"3a55ac034801d45a47ee542b4d631d6f","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn27@2020_2/2021/04/07/17-38-14-598_49c4aea15b116dde.webp","destWidth":590,"destHeight":393,"sourceBytes":47956,"destBytes":16206,"author":"","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://2.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS590x0~articles/3873565570/Canon_EOS_R5.jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn27@2020_2/2021/04/07/17-38-14-598_49c4aea15b116dde.webp","https://3.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS1180x0~articles/3873565570/C_Log_graph.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn82@2020_5/2021/04/07/17-38-32-088_f7d825498653d208.webp","https://2.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS1152x0~articles/3873565570/CLog-1_exp.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn39@2020_4/2021/04/07/17-38-33-021_c9e469a238d59ff5.webp","https://4.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS1152x0~articles/3873565570/CLog-1.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn7@2020_3/2021/04/07/17-38-32-751_c43d0232b05106f0.webp","https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS1180x0~articles/3873565570/Jordan_CL3_LUT.jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn16@2020_1/2021/04/07/17-38-32-024_e6ea5c07dfb8e252.webp","https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS1180x0~articles/3873565570/Jordan_CL1_LUT.jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn64@2020_1/2021/04/07/17-38-32-451_f0bf74199d5a149d.webp","https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS1180x0~articles/3873565570/Scene_CL3_LUT.jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx27/cdn64@2020_3/2021/04/07/17-38-31-906_1f69cd7ac966162c.webp","https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS1180x0~articles/3873565570/Scene_CL1_LUT.jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn83@2020_4/2021/04/07/17-38-48-926_10fb475aa5106063.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1617817093435},{"createdTime":"2021-04-08 01:38:13","updatedTime":"2021-04-08 01:38:13","title":"Backblaze reveals what hard drive models had the lowest failure rates in 2020","link":"https://www.dpreview.com/news/4389052919/backblaze-reveals-what-hard-drive-models-had-the-lowest-failure-rates-in-2020","description":"<table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCaptions noCrop singleNoBorder center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"590\"> \n <tbody> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 590px;\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"590\" height=\"374\" src=\"https://2.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS590x0~articles/4389052919/06DC64C0-8930-46F9-AFAA-35A99FCF7737.jpeg\" width=\"590\" data-filename=\"06DC64C0-8930-46F9-AFAA-35A99FCF7737.jpeg\" /></td> \n  </tr> \n </tbody> \n</table> \n<p>Cloud-based backup company <a href=\"http://backblaze.com/\">Backblaze</a> has <a href=\"https://www.backblaze.com/blog/backblaze-hard-drive-stats-for-2020/\">published</a> its full-year 2020 hard drive stats, revealing just how many hard drives in its data centers have failed over the past calendar year.</p> \n<p>According to Backblaze’s data, the company added 39,792 hard drives to its collection 2020, bringing the total to 165,530 drives. Of those, 3,000 were boot drives, while the remaining 162,530 were data drives. Backblaze excluded 231 of its data drives from its data, as they ‘were either used for testing or [Backblaze] did not have at least 60 drives of the same model at any time during the year.’ This means the following data is based on a total of 162,299 hard drives.</p> \n<p>As visible from the below graph, the Seagate 6TB drive (model: <a href=\"https://www.newegg.com/seagate-st6000dx000-6tb/p/N82E16822178737\">ST6000DX000</a>) has the lowest annualized failure rate of just 0.23%, with HGST’s 4TB drive (model: <a href=\"https://www.newegg.com/p/1Z4-001J-00206\">HMS5C4040ALE640</a>), 4TB drive (model: <a href=\"https://www.newegg.com/hgst-megascale-dc-4000-b-hms5c4040ble640-4tb/p/N82E16822145981\">HMS5C4040BLE640</a>), 8TB drive (model: <a href=\"https://www.newegg.com/hgst-ultrastar-he8-huh728080ale600-8tb/p/N82E16822145969\">HUH728080ALE600</a>) and 12TB drive (model: <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/HGST-Ultrastar-HUH721212ALE600-Platform-Enterprise/dp/B07CC48DYL\">HUH721212ALE600</a>) not far behind with annualized failure rates of 0.27%, 0.27%, 0.29% and 0.31%, respectively.</p> \n<table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCrop single center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"520\"> \n <tbody> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 520px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/4389052919/2F0473DF-FFB3-4E6F-948E-B0840FD9716B.jpeg\" target=\"article-93284cbc8f7b4f109fd0bd22b5cd8f9e\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"520\" height=\"641\" src=\"https://4.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS520x0~articles/4389052919/2F0473DF-FFB3-4E6F-948E-B0840FD9716B.jpeg\" width=\"520\" data-filename=\"2F0473DF-FFB3-4E6F-948E-B0840FD9716B.jpeg\" /></a></td> \n  </tr> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"caption\" style=\"width: 520px;\">Chart by Backblaze. Click to enlarge.</td> \n  </tr> \n </tbody> \n</table> \n<p>Backblaze says one of its goals going into 2020 was to diversify its hard drive lineup. This decision ‘proved to be prophetic in 2020, as the effects of Covid-19 began to creep into the world economy in March 2020.’ Specifically, Backblaze says its decision to diversify helped to ‘manage [its] supply chain through the manufacturing and shipping delays prevalent in the first several months of the pandemic.’</p> \n<p>As a whole, Backblaze’s annualized failure rates for 2020 was 0.93%, which is less than half the 1.89% annualized failure rate it incurred in 2019. Backblaze says this reduction was a ‘group effort’ that ultimately saw all drives, new and old, small and large, perform well in 2020.</p> \n<p>Backblaze further contextualizes its 2020 data with confidence intervals for each specific drive model and further dives into what specific drives it added to its lineup in 2020 in its <a href=\"https://www.backblaze.com/blog/backblaze-hard-drive-stats-for-2020/\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">blog post</a>. You can even download the raw data from Backblaze as a ZIP file with CSV files for each chart towards the bottom of the post.</p> \n<p>This data might not necessarily affect you if you aren’t a Backblaze user, but seeing drive failure rates from one of the largest cloud backup providers can help you better decide what drives might most be worth it for your personal storage solution, be it a single external hard drive or a dedicated RAID array.</p>","descriptionType":"text/html","publishedDate":"Wed, 07 Apr 2021 14:12:00 +0000","feedId":70,"bgimg":"https://2.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS590x0~articles/4389052919/06DC64C0-8930-46F9-AFAA-35A99FCF7737.jpeg","linkMd5":"b7a237b00c3c7a6e45ab56132ea52a55","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn29@2020_6/2021/04/07/17-38-14-565_7c528782e1cf67f5.webp","destWidth":590,"destHeight":374,"sourceBytes":81684,"destBytes":45868,"author":"","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://2.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS590x0~articles/4389052919/06DC64C0-8930-46F9-AFAA-35A99FCF7737.jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn29@2020_6/2021/04/07/17-38-14-565_7c528782e1cf67f5.webp","https://4.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS520x0~articles/4389052919/2F0473DF-FFB3-4E6F-948E-B0840FD9716B.jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn59@2020_1/2021/04/07/17-38-32-481_b691277c2e12f8bb.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1617817093461},{"createdTime":"2021-04-08 cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCaptions single center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"520\"> \n <tbody> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 520px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/4877731670/Instax-Mini-40-4.jpeg\" target=\"article-4877731670\"><img border=\"0\" data-aspect-ratio=\"4x3\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" /></a></td> \n  </tr> \n </tbody> \n</table> \n<p>We just got our hands on Fujifilm's new Instax Mini 40 model, a stylish and easy-to-use instant camera that uses the company's most popular Instax film format: Mini.</p> \n<p>Feature and spec-wise, this new model is identical to the Instax Mini 11 that launched just last year; read our full <a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/reviews/fujifilm-instax-mini-11-review-the-best-easy-to-use-instax-mini-model\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">Instax Mini 11 review</a> to learn more. But the Mini 40 is undoubtedly cooler and more retro-chic than its curvy cousin. But that cool factor comes at a slightly higher cost.</p> \n<p>Let's take a closer look at this new model.</p> \n<h2>Instax Mini 40 - design &amp; handling</h2> \n<table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCaptions single center\" data-image-height=\"\" data-image-width=\"520\"> \n <tbody> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 520px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/4877731670/Instax-Mini-40-5.jpeg\" target=\"article-4877731670\"><img border=\"0\" data-aspect-ratio=\"4x3\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"520\" height=\"390\" src=\"https://3.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TC4x3S520x0~articles/4877731670/Instax-Mini-40-5.jpeg\" width=\"520\" data-filename=\"Instax-Mini-40-5.jpeg\" /></a></td> \n  </tr> \n </tbody> \n</table> \n<p>The Mini 40's retro-inspired design, complete with silver detailing and faux black leather, reminds us of the higher-end <a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/reviews/buying-guide-best-instant-camera/7\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">Instax Mini 90</a>. The textured plastic leatherette provides a pleasing amount of 'grippyness'. And despite feeling a bit plasticky, nothing about the Mini 40 feels cheap.</p> \n<p>Size and weight-wise, the Mini 40 is a match for most other Instax Mini models, which is to say it's fairly lightweight and compact. However, it is a bit chunkier than the <a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/reviews/buying-guide-best-instant-camera/2\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">Instax Mini 70</a>, our pick for the <a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/reviews/buying-guide-best-instant-camera\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">best Instax camera in 2021</a>.</p> \n<h2>Instax Mini 40 - design &amp; handling cont.</h2> \n<table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCaptions single center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"520\"> \n <tbody> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 520px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/4877731670/Instax-Mini-40-2.jpeg\" target=\"article-4877731670\"><img border=\"0\" data-aspect-ratio=\"4x3\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"520\" height=\"390\" src=\"https://4.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TC4x3S520x0~articles/4877731670/Instax-Mini-40-2.jpeg\" width=\"520\" data-filename=\"Instax-Mini-40-2.jpeg\" /></a></td> \n  </tr> \n </tbody> \n</table> \n<p>The camera is operated in the vertical orientation. The viewfinder may feel a bit small, especially if you're used to looking through the finder of a modern digital camera, but that's par for the course with these Instax Mini models.</p> \n<p>A rear thumb rest is well-positioned and allows you to grip the camera comfortably and confidently. Below the thumb rest, on the film door, you'll find a frame counter indicating the remaining shots left on a pack of film.</p> \n<h2>Instax Mini 40: lens &amp; exposure capability</h2> \n<table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCaptions single center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"520\"> \n <tbody> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 520px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/4877731670/Instax-Mini-40-3.jpeg\" target=\"article-4877731670\"><img border=\"0\" data-aspect-ratio=\"4x3\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"520\" height=\"390\" src=\"https://1.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TC4x3S520x0~articles/4877731670/Instax-Mini-40-3.jpeg\" width=\"520\" data-filename=\"Instax-Mini-40-3.jpeg\" /></a></td> \n  </tr> \n </tbody> \n</table> \n<p>The Mini 40 utilizes the same retractable 35mm-equiv. F12.7 lens as the Mini 11. A press of the grey button (bottom right) both deploys the lens and turns the camera on. To turn the camera off, simply push the lens back in.</p> \n<p>The Mini 40 is fully automatic with a flash that always fires, and exposure is adjusted by the camera via a variable-speed shutter (1/2 - 1/250 sec). The maximum flash range is 2.7 m / 8.85 ft and the recycle time is about 6.5 secs. There's no need to set or adjust the focus with the Mini 40, it has a fixed focus range of 0.3 m to infinity.</p> \n<h2>Instax Mini 40 - selfie mode and mirror</h2> \n<table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCaptions single center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"520\"> \n <tbody> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 520px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/4877731670/Instax-Mini-40-9.jpeg\" target=\"article-4877731670\"><img border=\"0\" data-aspect-ratio=\"4x3\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"520\" height=\"390\" src=\"https://3.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TC4x3S520x0~articles/4877731670/Instax-Mini-40-9.jpeg\" width=\"520\" data-filename=\"Instax-Mini-40-9.jpeg\" /></a></td> \n  </tr> \n </tbody> \n</table> \n<p>Like some of its siblings, the Mini 40 offers a selfie/close-up mode that can be activated by pulling the front of the lens outward (which takes some force). Engaging this mode is supposed to improve sharpness as the lens' closeup range. But from our testing with the Mini 11, we've found it has little noticeable impact, compared to the normal focus mode.</p> \n<p>The Mini 40 also offers a small mirror on the front of the lens to assist in framing seflies.</p> \n<h2>Instax Mini 40 - film and battery life</h2> \n<table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCaptions single center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"520\"> \n <tbody> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 520px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/4877731670/Instax-Mini-40-6.jpeg\" target=\"article-4877731670\"><img border=\"0\" data-aspect-ratio=\"4x3\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"520\" height=\"390\" src=\"https://4.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TC4x3S520x0~articles/4877731670/Instax-Mini-40-6.jpeg\" width=\"520\" data-filename=\"Instax-Mini-40-6.jpeg\" /></a></td> \n  </tr> \n </tbody> \n</table> \n<p>The camera runs on two AA batteries which should provide enough juice for 100 shots, or 10 packs of Instax Mini film. Keep in mind though, the more depleted your batteries are, the longer the flash will take to recycle between shots.</p> \n<p>Instax Mini film is sold in single and double packs, as well as larger bulk packs including those with 60 and 100 exposures. To get the lowest cost per shot (~$0.50), we recommend splurging on the larger pack sizes upfront.</p> \n<h2>Instax Mini 40 - the wrap</h2> \n<table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCaptions single center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"520\"> \n <tbody> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 520px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/4877731670/Instax-Mini-40-8.jpeg\" target=\"article-4877731670\"><img border=\"0\" data-aspect-ratio=\"4x3\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"520\" height=\"390\" src=\"https://2.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TC4x3S520x0~articles/4877731670/Instax-Mini-40-8.jpeg\" width=\"520\" data-filename=\"Instax-Mini-40-8.jpeg\" /></a></td> \n  </tr> \n </tbody> \n</table> \n<p>Ultimately, the Instax Mini 40 combines the ease of use of the entry-level Mini 11 with the cool stylings of the upper-end Mini 90. The result is a camera we see appealing to a lot of folks – those who value simplicity but also want something fun-looking they can show off. In that regard, it is a welcomed addition to the Instax Mini family.</p> \n<p>Shipping at the end of April 2021, the Fujifilm Instax Mini 40 will retail for \n<p>On a 0–1 pitch in the top of the second inning, Alcantara delivered a 90mph (145kph) change-up that O’Neill fouled right into a camera behind home plate. Based on the broadcast footage, it appears as though he shattered the front elements of a <a href=\"https://www.bhphotovideo.com/c/product/475197-REG/Fujinon_WCV_L85_WCV_L85_0_8x_Wide_Converter.html\">Fujinon WCV-L85 0.8x Wide Angle Converter lens</a>, which was attached to the front of a <a href=\"https://www.bhphotovideo.com/c/product/1502012-REG/fujinon_ua18x7_6_4k_uhd_f1_8_lens.html\">Fujinon UA18x7.6BERD broadcast zoom lens</a>. While seeing the shattered elements of the destroyed wide-angle converter is still a little heartbreaking, it’s a little easier on the heart — and wallet — considering the adapter retails for $1,799, compared to the $22,495 price tag of the lens itself.</p> \n<p>The game was briefly delayed as the umpires called for the shattered glass to be cleaned up. The Cardinals would go on to win the game 4–2 against the Marlins, putting them up 2–0 in the series, which concludes with a game today.</p>","descriptionType":"text/html","publishedDate":"Wed, 07 Apr 2021 16:29:00 +0000","feedId":70,"bgimg":"https://4.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS590x0~articles/8625024771/66D00F15-E7E8-44DD-A670-7F103FEC0B1A.jpeg","linkMd5":"c994c8f14838e77db71d0fc4bc6c5851","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn41@2020_1/2021/04/07/17-38-14-295_ad7427c81894f0e2.webp","destWidth":590,"destHeight":331,"sourceBytes":39951,"destBytes":16278,"author":"","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://4.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS590x0~articles/8625024771/66D00F15-E7E8-44DD-A670-7F103FEC0B1A.jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn41@2020_1/2021/04/07/17-38-14-295_ad7427c81894f0e2.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1617817093461},{"createdTime":"2021-04-08 01:38:13","updatedTime":"2021-04-08 01:38:13","title":"This 3D-printed lens lets you create 'wigglegrams'","link":"https://www.dpreview.com/news/1238704821/this-3d-printed-lens-lets-you-create-wigglegrams","description":"<table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCaptions noCrop singleNoBorder center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"590\"> \n <tbody> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 590px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/1238704821/wiggle-lens-banner.jpeg\" target=\"article-f17e19d227384b2086a45f75c673a8bd\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"590\" height=\"199\" src=\"https://3.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS590x0~articles/1238704821/wiggle-lens-banner.jpeg\" width=\"590\" data-filename=\"wiggle-lens-banner.jpeg\" /></a></td> \n  </tr> \n </tbody> \n</table> \n<p>Designer and maker <a href=\"https://www.georgemoua.com/\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">George Moua</a> <a href=\"https://www.georgemoua.com/3d-wiggle-lens\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">has built</a> a bespoke 3D-printed 3D stereoscopic 'wiggle lens' for full-frame Sony E-mount cameras and APS-C Fujifilm X mount cameras. The 3D-printed lens allows compatible cameras to shoot stereoscopic wiggle photography. Essentially, by combining multiple frames shot with the lens, you can create a motion picture that appears to be 3D.</p> \n<p>Moua's stereoscopic wiggle lens incorporates a trio of 30mm lens to project three images with slightly different perspectives across the image sensor. The wiggle lens creates a parallax shift in between each frame, such that when you combine them into an animated sequence, there's a visual sense of depth in the animated frame.</p> \n<table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCrop singleNoBorder center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"590\"> \n <tbody> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 590px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/1238704821/wiggle-lens-full-frame-sony.jpeg\" target=\"article-f17e19d227384b2086a45f75c673a8bd\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"590\" height=\"387\" src=\"https://4.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS590x0~articles/1238704821/wiggle-lens-full-frame-sony.jpeg\" width=\"590\" data-filename=\"wiggle-lens-full-frame-sony.jpeg\" /></a></td> \n  </tr> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"caption\" style=\"width: 590px;\">George Moua's full-frame stereoscopic wiggle lens includes three lenses, which project a roughly 1:2 ratio image across the 3:2 aspect ratio image sensor.</td> \n  </tr> \n </tbody> \n</table> \n<p>The full-frame version, seen in Moua's video below, extends as far as possible into the lens mount without interfering with the shutter or IBIS mechanisms. However, the baffles can't touch the image sensor, so there is some slight light leakage in between each frame. This is easily corrected in post, as we'll see in a second video. The lens also uses a breech-lock mounting system rather than a standard bayonet lens mount, which means that the lens is attached to the camera using a rotating ring that tightens the lens to the body. Moua has also crafted a bayonet mount version, although it offers poorer performance.</p> \n<div class=\"video\">\n <iframe allowfullscreen=\"\" frameborder=\"0\" height=\"326\" id=\"videoFrame\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/flX9ZyU1X9A?rel=0&amp;autohide=1&amp;wmode=transparent&amp;enablejsapi=1\" width=\"580\"></iframe>\n</div> \n<p>Creating a wigglegram is not as simple as just capturing the image. Moua has created a video showing his workflow to create wigglegrams using Adobe Lightroom and Photoshop. Moua shoots with a Sony A7, so it's a 3:2 aspect ratio. Using a 1:2 crop ratio, Moua crops three frames from a single image. He exports each crop as a .DNG file and then imports them back into Lightroom. Once the individual frames are in Lightroom, he edits them such that they have the same appearance, as there is sometimes variation in brightness, contrast and color across the three frames. When the images are matched, he opens them as layers in Photoshop. To see how Moua creates a wigglegram in Photoshop, check out the tutorial below.</p> \n<div class=\"video\">\n <iframe allowfullscreen=\"\" frameborder=\"0\" height=\"326\" id=\"videoFrame\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/WltDW2eOjP4?rel=0&amp;autohide=1&amp;wmode=transparent&amp;enablejsapi=1\" width=\"580\"></iframe>\n</div> \n<p>Unfortunately, preorders for the full-frame Sony E-mount, APS-C E-mount and APS-C Fujifilm X mount stereoscopic wiggle lenses have sold out. However, Moua intends to make STL files available for sale once he has fulfilled his preorders. The lenses sold for $80 for the full-frame version and $70 for the APS-C versions. Moua will be using his profits to purchase a Canon EOS RP to finish work on a Canon full-frame version of his stereoscopic wiggle lens. He is going to work on a Nikon version down the road as well. For additional information, <a href=\"https://www.georgemoua.com/3d-wiggle-lens\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">click here</a>.</p>","descriptionType":"text/html","publishedDate":"Tue, 06 Apr 2021 20:02:00 +0000","feedId":70,"bgimg":"https://3.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS590x0~articles/1238704821/wiggle-lens-banner.jpeg","linkMd5":"9debcc50eaabd25cdca21b6bcf241bcc","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn34@2020_4/2021/04/07/17-38-14-511_52137cb6a257f407.webp","destWidth":590,"destHeight":199,"sourceBytes":33719,"destBytes":15976,"author":"","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://3.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS590x0~articles/1238704821/wiggle-lens-banner.jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn34@2020_4/2021/04/07/17-38-14-511_52137cb6a257f407.webp","https://4.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS590x0~articles/1238704821/wiggle-lens-full-frame-sony.jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn43@2020_2/2021/04/07/17-38-31-913_c5b94f04e0c46d2f.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1617817093461},{"createdTime":"2021-04-08 01:38:13","updatedTime":"2021-04-08 01:38:13","title":"Fujifilm introduces stylish Instax Mini 40 instant camera","link":"https://www.dpreview.com/news/7470390181/fujifilm-introduces-stylish-instax-mini-40-instant-camera","description":"<div id=\"embeddedSampleGallery_8178730731\" class=\"sampleGalleryImageViewerContainer\" style=\"height: 570px\"></div>\n<script type=\"text/javascript\">$(document).ready(function() { SampleGalleryV2({\"containerId\":\"embeddedSampleGallery_8178730731\",\"galleryId\":\"8178730731\",\"isEmbeddedWidget\":true,\"selectedImageIndex\":0,\"isMobile\":false}) });</script> \n<p>Fujifilm has introduced the retro-styled Instax Mini 40, its latest instant camera. Alongside the debut of MINI 40, Fujifilm introduces a new INSTAX MINI instant film variety, “Contact Sheet”, which mimics the look of a classic film contact sheet and adds a new twist to the popular INSTAX MINITM instant film series.</p> \n <p>“The new MINI 40 will appeal to sophisticated instant photo enthusiasts, whom have already been using our INSTAX product for years and are now looking for an instant camera with a timeless design,” said Manny Almeida, Division President, Imaging Division, FUJIFILM North America Corporation. “Designed to be easily portable, MINI 40 is finished with a high-quality texture that fits in one hand. The lustrous black camera body is accented with silver touches, resulting in a classic and chic look.”</p> \n <p><strong><span style=\"text-decoration: underline;\">Key MINI 40 features include</span>:</strong></p> \n <p><strong>Automatic Exposure function for better pictures any time of the day</strong></p> \n <p>The Automatic Exposure function automatically senses the level of ambient light when the shutter button is pressed, and optimizes the shutter speed and flash output according to the scene. It allows even novice INSTAX instant camera users to take photos that are automatically properly exposed regardless of interior or exterior conditions, producing high-quality photo prints on-the-spot.</p> \n <p><strong>Selfie Mode for quicker and easier selfies</strong></p> \n <p>Users can activate the Selfie Mode, perfect for taking selfies and close-up shots, by simply pulling out the front-end edge of the lens after powering the camera on. This makes it incredibly easy and convenient to take selfies and close-up pictures.</p> \n <p><strong>INSTAX MINI Contact Sheet instant film</strong></p> \n <p>Also accompanying the launch of MINI 40 is new INSTAX MINI Contact Sheet instant film. An homage to classic film photography, the design of the new instant film is inspired by a photographer’s contact sheet. As with all INSTAX MINI instant film, Contact Sheet will be available in a single pack with 10 exposures.</p> \n <p>MINI 40 joins a fun and versatile lineup of INSTAX instant cameras and Smartphone printers. Over 22,000 images were submitted from 73 countries. Finalists are competing for a £5,000 cash prize.</p> \n<div class=\"page\" title=\"Page 1\"> \n <div class=\"section\"> \n  <div class=\"layoutArea\"> \n   <div class=\"column\"> \n    <p>'This year we saw an incredible 22,000 entries into the competition, with images coming in from all over the world,' said Will Nicholls, wildlife cameraman and Director at Bird Photographer of the Year. 'The standard of photography was incredibly high, and the diversity in different species was great to see. Now the judges are going to have a tough time deciding the winner of the competition!'</p> \n   </div> \n  </div> \n </div> \n</div> \n<p>The winner will be announced on September 1st. All finalist images can be viewed on the <a href=\"https://www.birdpoty.com\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">BPOTY website</a>.</p> \n<h2>Finalist: 'Mallard Duck' by <a href=\"https://www.zdenekjakl.com\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">Zdeněk Jakl</a></h2> \n<table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCaptions noCrop single center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"520\"> \n <tbody> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 520px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/2282996842/BPOTY-2021-Finalists-20.jpeg\" target=\"article-b5d5696a56994f71932f7f91085d45e2\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"520\" height=\"347\" src=\"https://4.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS520x0~articles/2282996842/BPOTY-2021-Finalists-20.jpeg\" width=\"520\" data-filename=\"BPOTY-2021-Finalists-20.jpeg\" /></a></td> \n  </tr> \n </tbody> \n</table> \n<p><strong>Artist Statement:</strong> I took the photograph on a pond in a beautiful park in a quiet part of the city of Prague. As a family of Mallard ducklings swam past me, one of them began to chase a flying fly. It highlighted the fact that the instinct to feed is a powerful force even in the young, but of course the behavior itself was comical from a human perspective. Regardless of how you view what’s going on, it certainly makes for an interesting photograph and a moment in time in a duckling’s life captured for posterity.</p> \n<p><strong>Specs:</strong> Nikon Z6 with Sigma 500mm f/4 Sport lens. 500mm focal length; 1/1,600th second; f/5.6; ISO 500.</p> \n<h2>Finalist: 'Hooded Crane' by Taku Ono</h2> \n<table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCaptions noCrop single center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"520\"> \n <tbody> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 520px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/2282996842/BPOTY-2021-Finalists-29.jpeg\" target=\"article-b5d5696a56994f71932f7f91085d45e2\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"520\" height=\"346\" src=\"https://3.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS520x0~articles/2282996842/BPOTY-2021-Finalists-29.jpeg\" width=\"520\" data-filename=\"BPOTY-2021-Finalists-29.jpeg\" /></a></td> \n  </tr> \n </tbody> \n</table> \n<p><strong>Artist Statement:</strong> When I arrived at a well-known wintering haunt of Hooded Cranes in Japan it was disappointingly overcast. And what’s more I was about to go home. However, I realized that an area of the clouds was gradually dissipating as the sun rose, and I decided to stay a while - just in case.</p> \n<p>Almost miraculously, a streak of sunlight shone through and highlighted a small group of flying cranes. I thanked the cranes, beloved by Japanese people as \"the bird of happiness\", for bringing me this good luck!</p> \n<p><strong>Specs:</strong> Canon 7D with Canon 100-400mm f/4.5-5.6 II lens. 400mm focal length; 1/250th second; f/5.6; ISO 100.</p> \n<h2>Finalist: 'Gentoo Penguin' by <a href=\"https://www.instagram.com/tomschandy/?hl=en\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">Tom Schandy</a></h2> \n<table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCaptions noCrop single center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"520\"> \n <tbody> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 520px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/2282996842/BPOTY-2021-Finalists-9.jpeg\" target=\"article-b5d5696a56994f71932f7f91085d45e2\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"520\" height=\"314\" src=\"https://3.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS520x0~articles/2282996842/BPOTY-2021-Finalists-9.jpeg\" width=\"520\" data-filename=\"BPOTY-2021-Finalists-9.jpeg\" /></a></td> \n  </tr> \n </tbody> \n</table> \n<p><strong>Artist Statement:</strong> Gentoo Penguins began surfing long before the first humans latched on to this craze. This image was taken at Carcass Island on the Falkland Islands, where the birds have no option but to surf if they want to get ashore. If the waves are a decent size, you can see the birds ride or surf on the top of them. It is a thrilling behaviour to watch, and a rewarding one to capture photographically.</p> \n<p><strong>Specs:</strong> Canon 1DX Mark II, Canon 100-400mm f/4.5-5.6 II lens. 400mm focal length; 1/4,000th second; f/5.6; ISO 400.</p> \n<h2>Finalist: 'Swallow' by <a href=\"https://davewhitephoto.com\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">David White</a></h2> \n<table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCaptions noCrop single center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"520\"> \n <tbody> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 520px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/2282996842/BPOTY-2021-Finalists-22.jpeg\" target=\"article-b5d5696a56994f71932f7f91085d45e2\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"520\" height=\"399\" src=\"https://2.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS520x0~articles/2282996842/BPOTY-2021-Finalists-22.jpeg\" width=\"520\" data-filename=\"BPOTY-2021-Finalists-22.jpeg\" /></a></td> \n  </tr> \n </tbody> \n</table> \n<p><strong>Artist Statement:</strong> Swallows have to be one of my favourite birds, and my entire family await their return in spring with nervous excitement. Will they arrive this year....? Then there’s the joy of that flash of steely blue as they return to the same stable on the farm. The one where they nested last year, and many years before that.</p> \n<p>This photo was taken from inside the building, using a remote trigger to fire the camera, which was situated at a safe distance just outside the window. The aim was to time the image-capture to coincide with the Swallow flying through the window and I am proud to have achieved my goal.</p> \n<p><strong>Specs:</strong> Olympus EM1 Mark III with Olympus 12-100mm f/4 lens. 20mm focal length; 1/200th second; f/ 11; ISO 200.</p> \n<h2>Finalist: 'Red-billed Oxpecker' by <a href=\"https://danielaanger.com/genre/gallery/\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">Daniela Anger</a></h2> \n<table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCaptions noCrop single center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"520\"> \n <tbody> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 520px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/2282996842/BPOTY-2021-Finalists-7.jpeg\" target=\"article-b5d5696a56994f71932f7f91085d45e2\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"520\" height=\"346\" src=\"https://1.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS520x0~articles/2282996842/BPOTY-2021-Finalists-7.jpeg\" width=\"520\" data-filename=\"BPOTY-2021-Finalists-7.jpeg\" /></a></td> \n  </tr> \n </tbody> \n</table> \n<p><strong>Artist Statement:</strong> In the South Luangwa National Park you can watch a Hippo colony from a water-level hide. In addition to their human admirers, the water-loving mammals also receive a lot of attention from the local Red-billed Oxpeckers who seek a close encounter for more practical reasons.</p> \n<p>The birds and the Hippos have evolved a symbiotic relationship: the oxpeckers feed on external parasites and the Hippos benefit from the hygienic makeover. This image shows two oxpeckers sitting on a very relaxed Hippo: all parties seem entirely comfortable with the relationship.</p> \n<p><strong>Specs:</strong> Canon 5D Mark IV with Canon 500mm f/4 II lens and 1.4x teleconverter. 700mm focal length; 1/800th second; f/5.6; ISO 160.</p> \n<h2>Finalist: 'Atlantic Puffin' by <a href=\"https://www.oyvindpedersen.com\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">Øyvind Pedersen</a></h2> \n<table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCaptions noCrop single center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"520\"> \n <tbody> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 520px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/2282996842/BPOTY-2021-Finalists-5.jpeg\" target=\"article-b5d5696a56994f71932f7f91085d45e2\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"520\" height=\"325\" src=\"https://3.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS520x0~articles/2282996842/BPOTY-2021-Finalists-5.jpeg\" width=\"520\" data-filename=\"BPOTY-2021-Finalists-5.jpeg\" /></a></td> \n  </tr> \n </tbody> \n</table> \n<p><strong>Artist Statement:</strong> This photo was taken on the bird cliffs of Hornøya Island in Norway, back in April 2018. It shows two Puffins which started a brawl that continued down the snowy slope right in front of me. My goal for this trip was to try to get some images of fighting Puffins on snow and in that regard my quest was a success.</p> \n<p>I was really lucky and my patience and persistence paid off. These two Puffins battled for several minutes, with feathers and snow flying everywhere. It was a fantastic experience - for me, if not for the Puffins.</p> \n<p><strong>Specs:</strong> Nikon D500 with Nikon 500mm f/4 lens. 500mm focal length; 1/2,000th second; f/5.6; ISO 800.</p> \n<h2>Finalist: <a href=\"https://www.facebook.com/Li-Gábor-Wildlife-photography-105085207970772/photos/\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">Gábor Li</a></h2> \n<table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCaptions noCrop single center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"520\"> \n <tbody> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 520px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/2282996842/BPOTY-2021-Finalists-24.jpeg\" target=\"article-b5d5696a56994f71932f7f91085d45e2\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"520\" height=\"346\" src=\"https://4.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS520x0~articles/2282996842/BPOTY-2021-Finalists-24.jpeg\" width=\"520\" data-filename=\"BPOTY-2021-Finalists-24.jpeg\" /></a></td> \n  </tr> \n </tbody> \n</table> \n<p><strong>Artist Statement:</strong> Last summer, while on a family holiday in Croatia, I spent time photographing Shags. One of my goals was to take a photo of them underwater, but it was a lot harder than I first thought. Although they didn't care about me, when they were on land they were much more cautious when they were underwater.</p> \n<p>I didn't want to bother them so my tactic was patience. I waited in the water for hours, next to the rock where they were roosting and from which I assumed they would jump and submerge. But in contrast to my expectations, I found they swam away to find a group of fish and only then would they dive. I was starting to lose patience and almost gave up.</p> \n<p>However, eventually my persistence paid off: encouraged to dive by a nearby swimmer, one of the Shags jumped into the water in front of me and dived after a few meters. I followed the bird under the water and took a few pictures of it almost blindly. I was very happy with the result. My favorite thing about this image is that you can see the sparkly spot lit by the setting sun where the bird submerged.</p> \n<p><strong>Specs:</strong> Nikon D500 with Tokina 10-17mm f/3.5-4.5 lens. 16mm focal length; 1/400th second; f/5.6; ISO 400.</p> \n<h2>Finalist: 'White-tailed sea-eagle' by <a href=\"https://fahadphoto.com/about/\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">Fahad Alenezi</a></h2> \n<table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCaptions noCrop single center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"520\"> \n <tbody> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 520px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/2282996842/BPOTY-2021-Finalists-14.jpeg\" target=\"article-b5d5696a56994f71932f7f91085d45e2\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"520\" height=\"292\" src=\"https://3.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS520x0~articles/2282996842/BPOTY-2021-Finalists-14.jpeg\" width=\"520\" data-filename=\"BPOTY-2021-Finalists-14.jpeg\" /></a></td> \n  </tr> \n </tbody> \n</table> \n<p><strong>Artist Statement:</strong> In winter, food for most animals is in short supply in northern latitudes and many species, including this Red Fox, take greater risks than they would normally do to survive. In this photo a particularly bold fox has ventured close to an area where eagles were feeding. One White- tailed Sea-eagle took exception to the incursion and gave the fox what looks like a good slap with its wings. That’s an encounter I imagine the fox will never forget.</p> \n<p><strong>Specs:</strong> Canon 1DX Mark II with Canon 600mm f/4 III lens. 600mm focal length; 1/3,200th second; f/8; ISO 800.</p> \n<h2>Finalist: 'Emperor Penguins' by <a href=\"https://thomasvijayan.com\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">Thomas Vijayan</a></h2> \n<table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCaptions noCrop single center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"520\"> \n <tbody> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 520px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/2282996842/BPOTY-2021-Finalists-30.jpeg\" target=\"article-b5d5696a56994f71932f7f91085d45e2\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"520\" height=\"780\" src=\"https://1.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS520x0~articles/2282996842/BPOTY-2021-Finalists-30.jpeg\" width=\"520\" data-filename=\"BPOTY-2021-Finalists-30.jpeg\" /></a></td> \n  </tr> \n </tbody> \n</table> \n<p><strong>Artist Statement:</strong> The Emperor Penguin is the tallest and heaviest of its kind and is endemic to Antarctica. These flightless birds breed in the winter and after a courtship lasting several weeks, the female lays a single egg then leaves! Each penguin egg's father balances it on his feet and covers it with his brood pouch, a very warm layer of feathered skin designed to keep the egg cozy.</p> \n<p>There the males stand, for about 65 days, through icy temperatures, cruel winds, and blinding storms. Finally, after about two months, the females return from the sea, bringing food which they regurgitate to feed the now-hatched chicks. The males eagerly leave for their own fishing session at sea, and the mothers take charge of parental care for a while.</p> \n<p>As the young penguins grow, adults leave them in groups called crèches while they go off to fish. Five years later, if they survive their time at sea, those young penguins will return to become parents themselves. There is a reason for the timing of Emperor Penguins' hatching. By December, when the Antarctic weather has warmed somewhat, the ice the penguins occupy begins to break up, bringing open waters closer to the nesting sites.</p> \n<p>To take this image, I was lying flat on the ground. I did this because objects lower than penguin height are less intimidating to the birds. Consequently, they spent plenty of time beside me, meaning I could capture some beautiful shots. On this particular trip, I walked an average of eight hours each day in search of a perfect image.</p> \n<p><strong>Specs:</strong> Nikon D5 with Nikon 400mm f/2.8 lens. 400mm focal length; 1/5,000th second; f/3.5; ISO 280.</p> \n<h2>Finalist: Black-and-white Warbler' by <a href=\"http://rayhennessy.com\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">Raymond Hennessy</a></h2> \n<table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCaptions noCrop single center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"520\"> \n <tbody> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 520px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/2282996842/BPOTY-2021-Finalists-16.jpeg\" target=\"article-b5d5696a56994f71932f7f91085d45e2\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"520\" height=\"346\" src=\"https://1.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS520x0~articles/2282996842/BPOTY-2021-Finalists-16.jpeg\" width=\"520\" data-filename=\"BPOTY-2021-Finalists-16.jpeg\" /></a></td> \n  </tr> \n </tbody> \n</table> \n<p><strong>Artist Statement:</strong> Backlit by dawn light, the breath of this Black-and-White Warbler shows the subtle colors of the rainbow as it drifts off in the cold morning air. I noticed a small shaft of sunlight shining in the forest in an area frequented by this warbler. With an image in mind, I devoted time to my quest, in the hope the bird might land in the right spot. When it did and it sang I was so happy!</p> \n<p><strong>Specs:</strong> Nikon D4S with Nikon 500mm f/4 lens. 500mm focal length; 1/500th second; f/4; ISO 800.</p> \n<h2>Finalist: 'Red-crowned Crane' by <a href=\"https://www.instagram.com/dijuneliu/?hl=en\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">Li Ying Lou</a></h2> \n<table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCaptions noCrop single center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"520\"> \n <tbody> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 520px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/2282996842/BPOTY-2021-Finalists-4.jpeg\" target=\"article-b5d5696a56994f71932f7f91085d45e2\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"520\" height=\"292\" src=\"https://2.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS520x0~articles/2282996842/BPOTY-2021-Finalists-4.jpeg\" width=\"520\" data-filename=\"BPOTY-2021-Finalists-4.jpeg\" /></a></td> \n  </tr> \n </tbody> \n</table> \n<p><strong>Artist Statement:</strong> Red-crowned Crane pairs are faithful to one another throughout the year, and even during the winter months they engage in behaviour designed to strengthen the bond. Birds perform dual honking rituals and an elaborate dance, and this is much appreciated by photographers who make the pilgrimage to see them in Japan.</p> \n<p>In order to capture the mood and convey a sense of the occasion to those looking at this photograph, I rushed to the photographic site at dawn. On my eighth attempt, I finally did photographic justice to the calling birds, with their breath vaporised by the cold air.</p> \n<p><strong>Specs:</strong> Canon 1DX Mark ll with Canon 100-400mm f/4.5-5.6 II lens and 1.4x teleconverter. 560mm focal length; 1/1,600th; f/8; ISO 1,000.</p> \n<h2>Finalist: 'Great Grey Owl' by Scott Suriano</h2> \n<table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCaptions noCrop single center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"520\"> \n <tbody> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 520px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/2282996842/BPOTY-2021-Finalists-12.jpeg\" target=\"article-b5d5696a56994f71932f7f91085d45e2\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"520\" height=\"374\" src=\"https://1.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS520x0~articles/2282996842/BPOTY-2021-Finalists-12.jpeg\" width=\"520\" data-filename=\"BPOTY-2021-Finalists-12.jpeg\" /></a></td> \n  </tr> \n </tbody> \n</table> \n<p><strong>Artist Statement:</strong> While exploring the Northwoods of Minnesota, I found myself caught in a sudden heavy snow squall. Thinking that this weather episode might deter the Great Grey Owls from hunting, I considered packing it up and calling it a day. To my surprise, however, this particular owl took to the skies and began scanning the meadow for its next meal.</p> \n<p>With a sudden and acrobatic downward turn, it sliced through the heavy white flakes and crashed head first into the snow-blanketed field below. Within moments, I watched as it launched off into the distance with its freshly caught vole. It was a great reminder that to be successful you have to sometimes fully commit and dive in head first into the unknown.</p> \n<p><strong>Specs:</strong> Canon 1DX Mark II with Canon 400mm f/2.8 lens and 1.4x teleconverter. 560mm focal length; 1/1,250th second; f/4; ISO 1,250.</p> \n<h2>Finalist: 'European Shag' by <a href=\"https://www.brianmatthewsphoto.com\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">Brian Matthews</a></h2> \n<table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCaptions noCrop single center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"520\"> \n <tbody> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 520px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/2282996842/BPOTY-2021-Finalists-2.jpeg\" target=\"article-b5d5696a56994f71932f7f91085d45e2\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"520\" height=\"329\" src=\"https://4.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS520x0~articles/2282996842/BPOTY-2021-Finalists-2.jpeg\" width=\"520\" data-filename=\"BPOTY-2021-Finalists-2.jpeg\" /></a></td> \n  </tr> \n </tbody> \n</table> \n<p><strong>Artist Statement:</strong> Is there any food left? In this image, a hungry juvenile Shag literally dives down its mother throat for more fish rather than waiting for it to be fully regurgitated. It was taken on the Farne Islands, one of the most accessible 'Puffin Islands' in the UK. A short boat trip from Seahouses in Northumberland drops you into another world of Puffins, Guillemots and ravenous Shags. Spending time with this family I managed to get some great behavioural shots. The Farne Islands aren't just about Puffins!</p> \n<p><strong>Specs:</strong> Canon 1DX with Canon 500mm f/4 lens. 500mm focal length; 1/1,250th second; f/4; ISO 800.</p> \n<h2>Finalist: 'Southern Giant Petrel' by <a href=\"http://www.wildnature.no\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">Eirik Grønningsæter</a></h2> \n<table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCaptions noCrop single center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"520\"> \n <tbody> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 520px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/2282996842/BPOTY-2021-Finalists-31.jpeg\" target=\"article-b5d5696a56994f71932f7f91085d45e2\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"520\" height=\"390\" src=\"https://4.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS520x0~articles/2282996842/BPOTY-2021-Finalists-31.jpeg\" width=\"520\" data-filename=\"BPOTY-2021-Finalists-31.jpeg\" /></a></td> \n  </tr> \n </tbody> \n</table> \n<p><strong>Artist Statement:</strong> Southern Giant Petrels happily scavenge on dead seals or penguins or any other dead animal. Generally, they are opportunistic birds although they will sometimes also kill the birds themselves - even adult King Penguin, the carcass in this picture.</p> \n<p>The petrels are not afraid of people and so I carefully placed my camera inside the carcass of the penguin and waited for the bird to start eating. When it comes to food and feeding, Southern Giant Petrels are possessive birds, and this one is stretching its wings to ward off other petrels in the neighborhood.</p> \n<p><strong>Specs:</strong> Olympus E-PL5 with Lumix 8mm f/1.8 Fisheye. 8mm focal length; 1/1,600th second; f/5; ISO 800.</p> \n<h2>Finalist: 'Eurasian Jackdaw' by Amanda Cook</h2> \n<table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCaptions noCrop single center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"520\"> \n <tbody> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 520px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/2282996842/BPOTY-2021-Finalists-18.jpeg\" target=\"article-b5d5696a56994f71932f7f91085d45e2\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"520\" height=\"346\" src=\"https://3.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS520x0~articles/2282996842/BPOTY-2021-Finalists-18.jpeg\" width=\"520\" data-filename=\"BPOTY-2021-Finalists-18.jpeg\" /></a></td> \n  </tr> \n </tbody> \n</table> \n<p><strong>Artist Statement:</strong> It was an enchanting morning in May and I felt as though this Jackdaw and Fallow Deer were part of some childhood fairytale with the bird whispering a secret to the deer. In reality, the narrative was more ordinary and the Jackdaw was pinching hair from the deer’s back to use in nest building. I often go into Bushy Park at dawn and on this occasion it was wonderful to capture the uninhibited and natural interaction between these two creatures.</p> \n<p><strong>Specs:</strong> Nikon D850 with Nikon 70-300mm f/4.5-5.6 lens. 240mm focal length; 1/200th second; f/5.6; ISO 320.</p>","descriptionType":"text/html","publishedDate":"Tue, 06 Apr 2021 19:12:00 photography by Dan Bracaglia</em></p> \n<div class=\"rightFloatedBox\"> \n <a class=\"articleProductBadgeAndScore\" href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/reviews/fujifilm-x-e4-review/#conclusion\"><span class=\"badge\"><img src=\"https://3.img-dpreview.com/resources/images/award-silver-dark.png?v=5287\" alt=\"Silver Award\" title=\"Silver Award\" /></span> \n  <div class=\"scoreContainer\"> \n   <div class=\"score\">\n     85% \n   </div> \n   <div class=\"scoreTip\">\n     Overall score \n   </div> \n  </div> \n  <div class=\"link\">\n    Jump to conclusion \n   <span class=\"caret\"></span> \n  </div></a> \n</div> \n<p>The Fujifilm X-E4 is a lightweight, rangefinder-styled camera built around a 26MP APS-C sized sensor that uses the company's X-mount lineup of lenses. Billed as a fun-to-use and compact photographic companion, the X-E4 is the smallest X-mount camera on the market, encouraging you to keep it around wherever you go.</p> \n<p>With Fujifilm's latest sensor and processor combo, the X-E4 inherits a lot of the goodies from the most recent Fujifilm cameras, including updated autofocus, solid video specs and really impressive burst shooting rates. And if you're a JPEG shooter, you now have <em>eighteen</em> of Fujifilm's excellent film simulations to choose from.</p> \n<hr> \n <p class=\"newsLink\" id=\"top\">Jump to:</p> \n <p class=\"newsLink\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/reviews/fujifilm-x-e4-review-small-size-big-image-quality#whatsnew\">What's new </a> | <a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/reviews/fujifilm-x-e4-review-small-size-big-image-quality#compared\">How it compares</a> | <a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/reviews/fujifilm-x-e4-review-small-size-big-image-quality#bodyhandling\">Body and handling </a>| <a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/reviews/fujifilm-x-e4-review-small-size-big-image-quality#imagequality\">Image Quality </a>| <a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/reviews/fujifilm-x-e4-review-small-size-big-image-quality#autofocus\">Autofocus </a>| <a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/reviews/fujifilm-x-e4-review-small-size-big-image-quality#video\">Video </a>| <a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/reviews/fujifilm-x-e4-review-small-size-big-image-quality#conclusion\">Conclusion </a>| <a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/reviews/fujifilm-x-e4-review-small-size-big-image-quality#samples\">Samples </a>| <a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/reviews/fujifilm-x-e4-review/2\">Full specifications</a></p> \n <hr> \n  <table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCrop singleNoBorder center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"590\"> \n   <tbody> \n    <tr> \n     <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 590px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/0601644611/DSCF0099.jpeg\" target=\"article-0601644611\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"1180\" height=\"393\" src=\"https://3.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS1180x0~articles/0601644611/DSCF0099.jpeg\" width=\"590\" data-filename=\"DSCF0099.jpeg\" /></a></td> \n    </tr> \n    <tr> \n     <td class=\"caption\" style=\"width: 590px;\">We've always found the X-E series to be a fun companion for photo walks. Out-of-camera JPEG shot using the Provia or standard film simulation.<br><br>ISO 160 | 1/480 sec | F8 | Fujifilm XF 35mm F1.4 R<br><em>Photo: Carey Rose</em></br></br></br></td> \n    </tr> \n   </tbody> \n  </table> \n  <p>We've been fans of Fujifilm's X-E series going back to the original <a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/reviews/fujifilm-x-e1\">Fujifilm X-E1</a>. We enjoy the size, controls, and styling – and of course, the image quality. But since the release of the X-T3, the first Fujifilm camera to use the newer 26MP sensor, the X-E series has lagged behind the updates in other areas of Fujifilm's lineup, so we were glad to see the X-E4 announced with the latest tech.</p> \n  <h3>Key specifications:</h3> \n  <ul> \n   <li>26MP APS-C sensor with X-Trans color filter array</li> \n   <li>3.0\" tilting touchscreen with 1.62M dots (can tilt up 180 degrees)</li> \n   <li>2.36M-dot electronic viewfinder, 0.62x magnification</li> \n   <li>DCI 4K/30p, 4:2:0, 8-bit internal video recording (4:2:2 10-bit over HDMI out)</li> \n   <li>Full HD video at up to 240p, for 10x slow motion</li> \n   <li>8 fps burst shooting with mechanical shutter (20 fps with electronic)</li> \n   <li>CIPA rated to 460 shots per charge (NP-W126S battery pack)</li> \n   <li>121mm x 73mm x 33mm</li> \n   <li>364g (12.9oz)</li> \n  </ul> \n  <p>On the inside, the X-E4 is more or less a Fujifilm X-S10 (and therefore much of an X-T4) minus the image stabilization Does it have what it takes to be considered for your next camera purchase? Let's find out.</p> \n  <p>The X-E4 is available now at a price of $849 body-only, and $1,049 when kitted with the XF 27mm F2.8 II pancake prime lens.</p> \n  <hr> \n   <h2 id=\"whatsnew\" style=\"margin-top: 8%;\">What's new and how it compares</h2> \n   <table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCrop singleNoBorder center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"590\"> \n    <tbody> \n     <tr> \n      <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 590px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/0601644611/Product/Fujifilm-X-E4-Sensor.jpeg\" target=\"article-0601644611\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"1180\" height=\"393\" src=\"https://1.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS1180x0~articles/0601644611/Product/Fujifilm-X-E4-Sensor.jpeg\" width=\"590\" data-filename=\"Product/Fujifilm-X-E4-Sensor.jpeg\" /></a></td> \n     </tr> \n     <tr> \n      <td class=\"caption\" style=\"width: 590px;\">The 26MP sensor at the heart of the X-E4 is excellent, offering great dynamic range and fast readout speeds.</td> \n     </tr> \n    </tbody> \n   </table> \n   <p>Relative to the Fujifilm X-E3, the X-E4 brings a suite of updates, the most important of which is the latest 26MP X-Trans sensor and quad-core X-Processor 4. This means the image quality and, in some cases, performance of the X-E4 will be a match for the best that Fujifilm has to offer in its X-mount lineup. The camera's body and controls have also been slimmed down relative to its predecessor, but we'll delve into those details in the next section.</p> \n   <p>That 26MP sensor brings with it really solid image quality, a native base ISO of 160 (down from 200 on the X-E3), and super-fast readout speeds that let the X-E4 fire away images at 20 fps with the electronic shutter (or 30 fps if you opt for a 1.25x crop). You also get super-fast electronic shutter readout that tops out at 1/32,000 sec, which is handy for shooting wide-open in bright daylight if that's your thing.</p> \n   <div class=\"beer-slider-container\"> \n    <div id=\"slider2\" class=\"beer-slider\" data-beer-label=\"Classic Neg\"> \n     <img src=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS1180x0~articles/0601644611/DSCF0134.jpeg\"> \n      <div class=\"beer-reveal\" data-beer-label=\"Provia (standard)\"> \n       <img src=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS1180x0~articles/0601644611/DSCF0109.jpeg\" /> \n      </div></img> \n    </div> \n   </div> \n   <div class=\"caption\">\n     We've found that Fujifilm's film simulation options can really alter the 'feeling' of a scene. Out-of-camera JPEGs. \n    <br>ISO 640 | 1/32000 sec (yes, you read that right) | F1.4 | Fujifilm XF 35mm F1.4 R<br>Fujifilm's DR400 mode was enabled, which raises the effective base ISO from 160 to 640.</br></br> \n   </div> \n   <p>The quad-core processor keeps everything moving pretty swiftly, and though you'll want the fastest memory card you can afford for those bursts, you won't gain any benefits from faster UHS-II compatible cards with the camera's UHS-I slot (it's still a good investment to get the fastest UHS-I card you can, though). The X-E4 also comes loaded with Fujifilm's latest film simulations, including Eterna, which is a favorite for video recording, as well as Classic Neg. And being able to re-process Raw files in-camera to try out the different film simulations is a fun way to find what looks you like best.</p> \n   <p>You also get an updated autofocus system with phase-detection coverage extending nearly to the edges of the frame, as well as the improved tracking interface and performance we first saw on the X-T4. We've found it's a very capable AF system but may require some tuning to get the most out of it.</p> \n   <table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCrop singleNoBorder center\" data-image-height=\"\" data-image-width=\"590\"> \n    <tbody> \n     <tr> \n      <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 590px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/0601644611/Product/Fujifilm-X-E4-Headphone-Dongle.jpeg\" target=\"article-0601644611\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"1180\" height=\"393\" src=\"https://3.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS1180x0~articles/0601644611/Product/Fujifilm-X-E4-Headphone-Dongle.jpeg\" width=\"590\" data-filename=\"Product/Fujifilm-X-E4-Headphone-Dongle.jpeg\" /></a></td> \n     </tr> \n     <tr> \n      <td class=\"caption\" style=\"width: 590px;\">Fujifilm includes a USB-C to headphone port adapter in the box with the X-E4 for audio monitoring while shooting video.</td> \n     </tr> \n    </tbody> \n   </table> \n   <p>The video on the X-E4 is a match for the X-S10, meaning it's really solid. You're getting DCI 4K/30p footage without a crop, F-Log recording (8-bit internally, 10-bit to an external recorder), impressive slow-motion in Full HD, and capture aids like zebra warnings. You also get both headphone and microphone ports, using the included USB-C to headphone adapter. But that lack of in-body image stabilization will mean that, for handheld footage, you're going to want to make sure you pick up a stabilized lens to keep your shots steady.</p> \n   <hr> \n    <h2 id=\"compared\" style=\"margin-top: 8%;\">How it compares</h2> \n    <p>The X-E4 slots into a pretty competitive segment in the camera market; we consider its most direct competitors to be the Nikon Z50, the Sony a6400 and the Canon EOS M6 Mark II, all of which are within $50 USD of the X-E4's MSRP. All of these options use APS-C sensors, and none offer in-body image stabilization.</p> \n    <div class=\"contentTable\"> \n     <table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\"   <td width=\"20%\">No</td> \n       </tr> \n       <tr> \n        <th width=\"20%\">Mic / headphone socket</th> \n        <td class=\"hi\" width=\"20%\">Yes / Yes (with adapter)</td> \n        <td
