 <td width=\"20%\">403g (14.2oz)</td> \n        <td width=\"20%\">408g (14.4oz)</td> \n       </tr> \n      </tbody> \n     </table> \n    </div> \n    <p>As you can see, the X-E4 really offers a lot of bang for your buck in this market segment, coming in with at least competitive specs in every category (battery life is especially notable). It's worth mentioning, though, that for another $150 USD, you can get into Fujifilm's X-S10; that camera has very similar core features to the X-E4, but adds in-body image stabilization and a bigger grip. The tradeoff is that of course it's a larger camera, and the ergonomics and handling are strikingly different.</p> \n    <p><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/reviews/fujifilm-x-e4-review-small-size-big-image-quality#top\"><strong>Back to top</strong></a></p> \n    <hr> \n     <h2 id=\"bodyhandling\" style=\"margin-top: 8%;\">Body and handling</h2> \n     <table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCrop singleNoBorder center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"590\"> \n      <tbody> \n       <tr> \n        <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 590px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/0601644611/Product/Fujifilm-X-E4-Grip.jpeg\" target=\"article-0601644611\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"1180\" height=\"393\" src=\"https://3.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS1180x0~articles/0601644611/Product/Fujifilm-X-E4-Grip.jpeg\" width=\"590\" data-filename=\"Product/Fujifilm-X-E4-Grip.jpeg\" /></a></td> \n       </tr> \n       <tr> \n        <td class=\"caption\" style=\"width: 590px;\">Gone from previous X-E models is the minimal front grip; but the optional MHG-XE4 accessory grip shown here inspires some confidence single-handed shooting if you're not concerned about traveling as light as possible. the grip adds an Arca-style plate to the base of the camera, for easy mounting onto most tripod systems.</td> \n       </tr> \n      </tbody> \n     </table> \n     <p>Just as the X-E3 saw a slight diminishing of size and control points relative to the X-E2S, so does the X-E4 relative to the X-E3. You get a slightly smaller (though a touch heavier) camera body than the outgoing model. This is ostensibly for the purpose of being more pocket-friendly (though such a claim is obviously going to be pretty lens-dependent). With the new XF 27mm F2.8 R WR lens attached, the X-E4 is lighter than Fujifilm's own fixed-lens X100V.</p> \n     <p>In use, we found that the camera itself is reasonably comfortable in the hand with just a wrist strap as long as you're sticking to a compact lens. If you're eyeing larger lenses, the optional MHG-X34 nor TR-XE4 thumb rest will help. Just don't expect ultimate comfort from a camera whose shape resembles a large bar of soap.</p> \n     <table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images singleNoBorder center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"590\"> \n      <tbody> \n       <tr> \n        <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 590px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/0601644611/Product/Fujifilm-X-E4-Top-03.jpeg\" target=\"article-0601644611\"><img border=\"0\" data-aspect-ratio=\"4x3\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"590\" height=\"442\" src=\"https://2.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TC4x3S590x0~articles/0601644611/Product/Fujifilm-X-E4-Top-03.jpeg\" width=\"590\" data-filename=\"Product/Fujifilm-X-E4-Top-03.jpeg\" /></a></td> \n       </tr> \n       <tr> \n        <td class=\"caption\" style=\"width: 590px;\">The X-E4 is the first X-E series camera to offer a tilting screen, which sits flush with the rear of the camera when folded away.</td> \n       </tr> \n      </tbody> \n     </table> \n     <p>But really, the X-E4 is a very attractive little camera. The faux leatherette looks and feels nice, the magnesium-alloy top plate is lovely and the camera body feels solid. The fold-flush rear screen is a real joy, and makes the X-E4 much easier to work with at high and low angles than its predecessor. A threaded shutter button is always a nice touch, and the dials have just the right amount of resistance.</p> \n     <p>Unfortunately, Fujifilm makes no claims of any weather resistance on the X-E4, despite doing so for its XF 27mm F2.8 R WR kit lens. On our test model at least, the 'Menu/OK' and 'Disp/Back' buttons on the rear plate are a little too mushy and a little too shallow. It'd also be nice if the shutter speed dial could spin 360 degrees like the exposure comp dial; once you hit 'P' or 'B', you can't keep turning it.</p> \n     <table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCaptions noCrop twoBottom center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"250\"> \n      <tbody> \n       <tr> \n        <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 250px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/0601644611/Product/Fujifilm-X-E4-front.jpeg\" target=\"article-0601644611\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"250\" height=\"167\" src=\"https://1.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS250x0~articles/0601644611/Product/Fujifilm-X-E4-front.jpeg\" width=\"250\" data-filename=\"Product/Fujifilm-X-E4-front.jpeg\" /></a></td> \n        <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 250px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/0601644611/Product/Fujifilm-X-E4-rear.jpeg\" target=\"article-0601644611\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"250\" height=\"167\" src=\"https://4.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS250x0~articles/0601644611/Product/Fujifilm-X-E4-rear.jpeg\" width=\"250\" data-filename=\"Product/Fujifilm-X-E4-rear.jpeg\" /></a></td> \n       </tr> \n      </tbody> \n     </table> \n     <p>We're not personally sold on the disappearance of the 'M-C-S' ('Manual,' 'Continuous' and 'Single') focus mode control which was on the front of the X-E2. This switch was a quick way to adjust a major autofocus setting depending on your subject matter, and since Fujifilm's autofocus system has historically benefitted from a bit more involvement on the part of the photographer in our testing, we're sad to see it go.</p> \n     <p>At least you can now assign autofocus modes and area settings to a custom setting bank to assign to a button for quick toggling, but again, you're low on buttons to which you can assign an 'access custom settings banks' function. The rear dial from the X-E3 has also been omitted, which does leave more room for your thumb, but again, it's one less control point.</p> \n     <blockquote class=\"pullQuote\">\n       I wonder whether Fujifilm went a little too minimalist on the X-E4 \n     </blockquote> \n     <p>The viewfinder is par for the course for this class of cameras, though not outstanding. The bigger issue is that, even though you'll want to press the Drive/Delete button with your left thumb, you'll almost certainly trigger the eye sensor to switch from the rear screen to using the EVF. It's a pain. And while the camera doesn't automatically switch to the EVF when you trigger the sensor with the screen tilted out, it does rotate the screen 180 degrees; the info display is flipped to seemingly prepare you for taking a selfie.</p> \n     <table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCrop singleNoBorder center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"590\"> \n      <tbody> \n       <tr> \n        <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 590px;\"><span class=\"green\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/0601644611/Product/Fujifilm-X-E4-EVF.jpeg\" target=\"article-0601644611\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"1180\" height=\"393\" src=\"https://2.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS1180x0~articles/0601644611/Product/Fujifilm-X-E4-EVF.jpeg\" width=\"590\" data-filename=\"Product/Fujifilm-X-E4-EVF.jpeg\" /></a></span></td> \n       </tr> \n       <tr> \n        <td class=\"caption\" style=\"width: 590px;\">The 2.36M-dot resolution of the X-E4's viewfinder is par for the segment; some users might find the 0.62x magnification on the small side.</td> \n       </tr> \n      </tbody> \n     </table> \n     <p>Basically, we're wondering whether Fujifilm went a little <em>too</em> minimalist on the X-E4. It took us a while to get it set up to where we could easily access all of the settings we want (and there are <em>lots</em> of things to assign to buttons, just not lots of buttons). In the end, we enabled the touch-swipe for custom functions to get a little more control, meaning you can swipe up, down, left or right on the rear screen to trigger a function. It works pretty well.</p> \n     <p>Lastly, Fujifilm's Auto ISO behavior is unchanged, meaning that you can set upper and lower bounds on ISO values, and then either specify a minimum shutter speed threshold or select 'Auto.' But there's still no way to bias 'Auto' to be faster or slower than half the focal length, as you can on most other competitors. On the other hand, you do get three banks of separate Auto ISO settings you can quickly swap between.</p> \n     <table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCaptions noCrop singleNoBorder center\" data-image-height=\"\" data-image-width=\"590\"> \n      <tbody> \n       <tr> \n        <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 590px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/0601644611/Product/Fujifilm-X-E4-Top.jpeg\" target=\"article-0601644611\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"1180\" height=\"393\" src=\"https://4.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS1180x0~articles/0601644611/Product/Fujifilm-X-E4-Top.jpeg\" width=\"590\" data-filename=\"Product/Fujifilm-X-E4-Top.jpeg\" /></a></td> \n       </tr> \n      </tbody> \n     </table> \n     <p>The X-E4 also has a new 'P' mode on its shutter speed dial. Selecting it will override whatever the lens's aperture ring is set to, and will put the camera into the Program Automatic mode. You can accomplish the same thing by setting both the aperture and shutter speed dials to 'A'.</p> \n     <h3>Battery and storage</h3> \n     <table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCaptions noCrop singleNoBorder center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"590\"> \n      <tbody> \n       <tr> \n        <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 590px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/0601644611/Product/Fujifilm-X-E4-battery.jpeg\" target=\"article-0601644611\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"1180\" height=\"393\" src=\"https://2.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS1180x0~articles/0601644611/Product/Fujifilm-X-E4-battery.jpeg\" width=\"590\" data-filename=\"Product/Fujifilm-X-E4-battery.jpeg\" /></a></td> \n       </tr> \n      </tbody> \n     </table> \n     <p>The Fujifilm X-E4 uses a familiar NP-W126S battery pack to achieve a CIPA-rated 460 shots per charge. As with most cameras, this is likely to be an underestimate in real-world use (how often do <em>you</em> shoot with flash and then immediately enter playback?), but it gives a reliable measure of <em>comparability</em> among competitive cameras.</p> \n     <p>This rating should easily get you through a weekend's worth of casual shooting should you be on holiday (hopeful thoughts for the future). And, probably thanks to increased processing efficiencies, the X-E4's rating puts it at the front of its pack in this regard. You can also charge the battery via the camera's USB-C port.</p> \n     <blockquote class=\"pullQuote\">\n       The UHS-I slot means you won't get any speed benefits if you use faster UHS-II cards \n     </blockquote> \n     <p>The X-E4 uses SD cards for storage; they're inexpensive and ubiquitous, but the X-E4 only supports UHS-I speeds. You can of course use UHS-II cards in the camera, you just won't see any performance benefit beyond a certain point.</p> \n     <p>Informal testing with a SanDisk Extreme Pro UHS-I U3 card shows that you can shoot losslessly compressed Raw and Fine JPEG images for between 1 and 1.5 seconds of burst shooting at 20fps, and wait then a little under 10 seconds for the buffer to clear. Shooting JPEG-only gets you around 2.5 seconds of shooting before the buffer fills, and then it clears after around 8 seconds.</p> \n     <p><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/reviews/fujifilm-x-e4-review-small-size-big-image-quality#top\"><strong>Back to top</strong></a></p> \n     <hr> \n      <h2 id=\"imagequality\" style=\"margin-top: 8%;\">Image Quality</h2> \n      <table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCrop singleNoBorder center\" data-image-height=\"\" data-image-width=\"590\"> \n       <tbody> \n        <tr> \n         <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 590px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/0601644611/DSCF0295.jpeg\" target=\"article-0601644611\"><img border=\"0\" data-aspect-ratio=\"4x3\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"590\" height=\"443\" src=\"https://3.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TC4x3S590x0~articles/0601644611/DSCF0295.jpeg\" width=\"590\" data-filename=\"DSCF0295.jpeg\" /></a></td> \n        </tr> \n        <tr> \n         <td class=\"caption\" style=\"width: 590px;\"> <p>The X-E4 offers a wide range of JPEG color profiles – both color and B&amp;W – meant to emulate traditional analog film stocks. This image was shot using the 'Acros' profile, a staff favorite. Out-of-camera JPEG. <br><br>ISO 160 | 1/1000 sec | F4 | XF 27mm F2.8 R WR<br><em>Photo Dan Bracaglia </em></br></br></br></p> </td> \n        </tr> \n       </tbody> \n      </table> \n      <p>Our <a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/articles/4553555371/introducing-the-test-scene\" target=\"article-5497708999\">test scene is designed to simulate</a> a variety of textures, colors and detail types you'll encounter in the real world. It also has two illumination modes to see the effect of different lighting conditions.</p> \n      <div id=\"reviewImageComparisonWidget-58888802\" class=\"imageComparisonContainer\"></div> \n      <script type=\"text/javascript\">$(document).ready(function() { ImageComparisonWidget({\"containerId\":\"reviewImageComparisonWidget-58888802\",\"widgetId\":810,\"initialStateId\":null}) })</script> \n      <p>The X-E4 uses the same 26MP APS-C sensor and quad-core X-Processor 4 as its flagship cousin, the <a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/reviews/fujifilm-x-t4-review/6\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">Fujifilm X-T4</a>, and is capable of the same outstanding image quality. Raw files show <span class=\"linkish imageComparisonLink\" id=\"icl-5401-77044630\">good detail capture</span><script type=\"text/javascript\">$(document).ready(function() { $(\"#icl-5401-77044630\").click(function() { ImageComparisonWidgetLink(5401); }); })</script>, competitive with other top APS-C cameras, though bested slightly by the higher-res EOS M6 II. <span class=\"linkish imageComparisonLink\" id=\"icl-5402--1537530301\">Noise levels</span><script type=\"text/javascript\">$(document).ready(function() { $(\"#icl-5402--1537530301\").click(function() { ImageComparisonWidgetLink(5402); }); })</script> at high ISOs are also comparable to the camera's closest and best competitors.</p> \n      <p><span class=\"linkish imageComparisonLink\" id=\"icl-5403-301621868\">Default JPEG color</span><script type=\"text/javascript\">$(document).ready(function() { $(\"#icl-5403-301621868\").click(function() { ImageComparisonWidgetLink(5403); }); })</script> from the X-E4 (shot using the 'Provia / Standard' profile) looks pleasing. The rendering of yellow tones in particular is spot-on; where some brands struggle with a slight greenish or orange hue in their yellows, Fujifilm does not. Greens and blues also look nicely saturated and accurate. Reds tones look accurate, but they aren't quite as well-saturated as Canon, Sony or Nikon reds. <span class=\"linkish imageComparisonLink\" id=\"icl-5413--1811740553\">Pink tones</span><script type=\"text/javascript\">$(document).ready(function() { $(\"#icl-5413--1811740553\").click(function() { ImageComparisonWidgetLink(5413); }); })</script> are more saturated/pinker than Canon and Sony's offerings, which could result in skin tones for some folks looking a bit off.</p> \n      <p><span class=\"linkish imageComparisonLink\" id=\"icl-5405-1453109520\">Default sharpening</span><script type=\"text/javascript\">$(document).ready(function() { $(\"#icl-5405-1453109520\").click(function() { ImageComparisonWidgetLink(5405); }); })</script> at lower ISOs is not quite as sophisticated as some of its competitors, namely the Sony. But at <span class=\"linkish imageComparisonLink\" id=\"icl-5406--2061945612\">high ISOs</span><script type=\"text/javascript\">$(document).ready(function() { $(\"#icl-5406--2061945612\").click(function() { ImageComparisonWidgetLink(5406); }); })</script> the X-E4 does a good job balancing noise reduction with detail retention.</p> \n      <h2>Dynamic range</h2> \n      <p>The X-E4 offers excellent Raw dynamic range for its sensor size, providing ample processing latitude for post-work. It uses the same dual gain style sensor as the flagship X-T4 which switches its gain 'mode' when the ISO hits 800.</p> \n      <p>In the lower mode you get maximum DR, but Raw files that are a bit noisier when brightened than those shot natively using the upper gain mode. At the upper gain mode, the sensor prioritizes low noise levels, at the cost of some dynamic range.</p> \n      <p><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/reviews/image-comparison/fullscreen?attr134_0=fujifilm_xe4&amp;attr134_1=fujifilm_xe4&amp;attr134_2=fujifilm_xe4&amp;attr134_3=fujifilm_xe4&amp;attr136_0=18&amp;attr136_1=40&amp;attr136_2=15&amp;attr136_3=13&amp;normalization=full&amp;widget=762&amp;x=0.15125082555145924&amp;y=0.4950670015347102\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">Brightened ISO 160 images</a> look a bit noisier than their native ISO 3200 output, but it's not a huge difference. This suggests the camera is adding very little noise, even in the lower gain mode. In practical terms, this means you can <a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/reviews/image-comparison/fullscreen?attr144_0=fujifilm_xe4&amp;attr144_1=sony_a6400&amp;attr144_2=oly_em5iii&amp;attr144_3=nikon_z50&amp;attr146_0=160_5&amp;attr146_1=100_5&amp;attr146_2=200_4&amp;attr146_3=100_5&amp;attr404_2=1&amp;normalization=compare&amp;widget=761&amp;x=0.15401536455468195&amp;y=0.5010148473543139\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">lower your ISO</a> when shooting high contrast scenes, as a means of reducing exposure/preserving highlights, without facing much of a noise penalty when lightening shadows in post. However, users who want the absolute cleanest noise levels from this camera should shoot at ISO 800.</p> \n      <p class=\"newsLink\"><strong><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/reviews/image-comparison/fullscreen?attr134_0=fujifilm_xe4&amp;attr134_1=fujifilm_xe4&amp;attr134_2=fujifilm_xe4&amp;attr134_3=fujifilm_xe4&amp;attr136_0=18&amp;attr136_1=40&amp;attr136_2=15&amp;attr136_3=13&amp;normalization=full&amp;widget=762&amp;x=0.15125082555145924&amp;y=0.4950670015347102\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">ISO invariance</a> | <a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/reviews/image-comparison/fullscreen?attr144_0=fujifilm_xe4&amp;attr144_1=sony_a6400&amp;attr144_2=oly_em5iii&amp;attr144_3=nikon_z50&amp;attr146_0=160_5&amp;attr146_1=100_5&amp;attr146_2=200_4&amp;attr146_3=100_5&amp;attr404_2=1&amp;normalization=compare&amp;widget=761&amp;x=0.15401536455468195&amp;y=0.5010148473543139\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">Exposure latitude </a></strong></p> \n      <p><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/reviews/fujifilm-x-e4-review-small-size-big-image-quality#top\"><strong>Back to top</strong></a></p> \n      <hr> \n       <h2 id=\"autofocus\" style=\"margin-top: 8%;\">Autofocus</h2> \n       <table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCrop singleNoBorder center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"590\"> \n        <tbody> \n         <tr> \n          <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 590px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/0601644611/Samples/1322911787.jpeg\" target=\"article-0601644611\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"1180\" height=\"393\" src=\"https://4.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS1180x0~articles/0601644611/Samples/1322911787.jpeg\" width=\"590\" data-filename=\"Samples/1322911787.jpeg\" /></a></td> \n         </tr> \n         <tr> \n          <td class=\"caption\" style=\"width: 590px;\">The X-E4's AF point coverage – identical to that of the flagship X-T4 – is ample and users can easily move their AF point/region via a responsive AF joystick on the back. <br>Out-of-camera JPEG. <br><br>ISO 320 | 1/320 sec | F2.8 | XF 16mm F2.8 R <em>WR</em><br><em>Photo: Carey Rose </em></br></br></br></br></td> \n         </tr> \n        </tbody> \n       </table> \n       <h3>Autofocus overview</h3> \n       <p>The autofocus implementation, behavior and performance of the X-E4 is identical to that of the <a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/reviews/fujifilm-x-t4-review/7\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">flagship X-T4</a>. Users can choose from a variety of focus modes including a single point, a cluster of points, or the full AF region. In AF-C, a subject tracking mode gives users the ability to place an AF box over their chosen subject, initiate AF via shutter half-press and/or the 'AFL' button, and track said subject around the frame.</p> \n       <p>There's also a face and eye-detect feature that can be turned on separately when using any of the AF modes. When a face is detected, a box will appear over it; a separate smaller box will appear over a detected eye. When multiple faces or eyes are detected in a scene, a tap of the AF joystick allows users to jump between them. Tapping the AF joystick away from a detected face/eye will also allow you to disengage face/eye detection and revert to the initially selected AF mode.</p> \n       <h3>Autofocus performance</h3> \n       <table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCrop singleNoBorder center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"590\"> \n        <tbody> \n         <tr> \n          <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 590px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/0601644611/Samples/DSCF0311.jpeg\" target=\"article-0601644611\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"1180\" height=\"393\" src=\"https://2.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS1180x0~articles/0601644611/Samples/DSCF0311.jpeg\" width=\"590\" data-filename=\"Samples/DSCF0311.jpeg\" /></a></td> \n         </tr> \n         <tr> \n          <td class=\"caption\" style=\"width: 590px;\">Unlike some of the competition, Fujifilm does not currently offer an 'Animal Eye AF' mode. No problem, we photographed Belvedere using a single point in AF-C. <br>Out-of-camera JPEG. <br><br>ISO 2500| 1/200 sec | F4 | XF 27mm F2.8 R WR <br><em>Photo Dan Bracaglia</em></br></br></br></br></td> \n         </tr> \n        </tbody> \n       </table> \n       <p>In most shooting scenarios, we found using a single point in AF-C to be the most reliable way to achieve critical focus. That said, for mostly static subjects, the subject-tracking AF mode also does a very good job in terms of reliability.</p> \n       <p>Face/eye detection also works reasonably well in most shooting scenarios, but this feature can occasionally give false positives, or shots that appear to have been captured sharp, but are in fact, slightly mis-focused. For casual users, this feature should be good enough. But if you're a pixel peeper or portrait professional, we wouldn't rely on it to nail focus every time.</p> \n       <p>When using a continuous burst to photograph fast-moving subjects, like athletes or wildlife, we also recommend using a single point or zone in AF-C – moved via AF joystick – to maintain focus. In our testing at both 8 fps (the top mechanical burst) and 20 fps (the top e-shutter burst), the X-E4 had no problem maintaining focus on a cyclist approaching the camera in a straight line, with a close to perfect hit rate.</p> \n       <table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCrop\" data-image-height=\"\" data-image-width=\"576\"> \n        <tbody> \n         <tr> \n          <td class=\"image\" colspan=\"10\" style=\"width: 590px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/0601644611/autofocus/weave1/XE4-01.jpeg\" target=\"article-0601644611\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"1152\" height=\"384\" id=\"weave\" src=\"https://3.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS1152x0~articles/0601644611/autofocus/weave1/XE4-01b.jpeg\" width=\"576\" data-filename=\"autofocus/weave1/XE4-01b.jpeg\" /></a></td> \n         </tr> \n         <tr> \n          <td class=\"caption imageSwapper active\" style=\"width: 10%; text-align: center;\" data-image-id=\"weave\" data-image-src=\"https://3.img-dpreview.com/files/p/articles/0601644611/autofocus/weave1/XE4-07b.jpeg?v=5287\" data-large-image-src=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/0601644611/autofocus/weave1/XE4-07.jpeg\"> <p class=\"newsLink\">7</p> </td> \n          <td class=\"caption imageSwapper\" style=\"width: 10%; text-align: center;\" data-image-id=\"weave\" data-image-src=\"https://1.img-dpreview.com/files/p/articles/0601644611/autofocus/weave1/XE4-09b.jpeg?v=5287\" data-large-image-src=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/0601644611/autofocus/weave1/XE4-09.jpeg\"> <p class=\"newsLink\">9</p> </td> \n          <td class=\"caption imageSwapper\" style=\"width: 10%; text-align: center;\" data-image-id=\"weave\" data-image-src=\"https://1.img-dpreview.com/files/p/articles/0601644611/autofocus/weave1/XE4-10b.jpeg?v=5287\" data-large-image-src=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/0601644611/autofocus/weave1/XE4-10.jpeg\"> <p class=\"newsLink\">10</p> </td> \n         </tr> \n        </tbody> \n       </table> \n       <div class=\"caption\">\n         In our above 'weave' test, we assess a camera's AF tracking performance by having a cyclist weave toward the camera in a manner that is difficult for it to predict. In a similar fashion to the X-T4, the X-E4 struggles with hunting throughout the weave. This test was shot using a tripod-mounted XF 50-140mm F2.8 R WR lens at 135mm. \n       </div> \n       <p>However, we had a less than perfect hit rate when photographing erratically moving subjects, approaching the camera, using the X-E4's AF subject tracking mode.</p> \n       <p>While performing the above bike weave test, in which we challenge a camera to identify a subject and then use the correct focus points to follow and maintain focus, we observed the camera tended to get easily distracted by elements in the background – especially bright colors – jumping off our subject, before returning several shots later. We also noticed the X-E4 tended to be slightly behind our subject when using AF tracking. And while tweaking the camera's 'AF-C custom settings' can lead to slight hit-rate improvements, for best results with fast/erratic subjects, we'd skip the AF tracking mode altogether and stick to a point or zone.</p> \n       <p><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/reviews/fujifilm-x-e4-review-small-size-big-image-quality#top\"><strong>Back to top</strong></a></p> \n       <hr> \n        <h2 id=\"video\" style=\"margin-top: 8%;\">Video</h2> \n        <table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCaptions noCrop singleNoBorder center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"590\"> \n         <tbody> \n          <tr> \n           <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 590px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/0601644611/Product/Fujifilm-X-E4-Video.jpeg\" target=\"article-0601644611\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"1180\" height=\"393\" src=\"https://2.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS1180x0~articles/0601644611/Product/Fujifilm-X-E4-Video.jpeg\" width=\"590\" data-filename=\"Product/Fujifilm-X-E4-Video.jpeg\" /></a></td> \n          </tr> \n         </tbody> \n        </table> \n        <h3>Video overview</h3> \n        <p>The X-E4 may not be an obvious choice for video work, given its rangefinder-style body, but it is actually quite capable. In terms of output, it can shoot oversampled DCI and UHD 4K video in 24 or 30 fps (30-minute cap on continuous capture). Full HD video can be captured at up to a whopping 240 fps.</p> \n        <p>The camera offers internal 8-bit Log capture and external 10-bit Log output (via the Micro-HDMI port) to a dedicated capture device (like an Atomos Ninja). For those wishing to avoid the fuss of color-grading in post, the Eterna/Cinema profile might be just what you need, offering flat contrast and rich tones.</p> \n        <div class=\"video\"> \n         <iframe allowfullscreen=\"\" frameborder=\"0\" height=\"326\" id=\"videoFrame\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/rrdvhuIuoiI?rel=0&amp;autohide=1&amp;wmode=transparent&amp;enablejsapi=1\" width=\"580\"></iframe> \n        </div> \n        <div class=\"caption\">\n          Jump to \n         <a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/videos/0943385178/dpreview-tv-fujifilm-x-e4-review#\">video performance</a> in our DPReviewTV video review, above. \n        </div> \n        <p>AF modes are limited when shooting video, compared to stills. While you still get face and eye-detection for human subjects, the standard autofocus subject tracking mode – where you place an AF box over your subject and initiate AF to lock-on – is absent. Face and eye detect work ok, but can occasionally the camera will lose the subject, leading to a focus rack.</p> \n        <p>There's no dedicated video record button, though one of the three custom buttons can be assigned to this function. To capture video out-of-the-box, you'll need to switch to video mode via the 'drive' button and hit the shutter release. The body has a full-size microphone port and an included USB-C-to-audio jack provides support for audio monitoring; you can adjust audio levels and add wind or low cut filters from within the camera's menus.</p> \n        <p>It's worth reiterating that, unlike the its oh-so-similar SLR-style sibling,<a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/reviews/fujifilm-x-s10-review#Video\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\"> the X-S10</a>, the X-E4 has no in-body image stabilization to aid in hand-held shooting (nor is there any form of digital IS). So if you're already tempted by the X-E4, but like shooting video, the X-S10 may be a better choice for you.</p> \n        <h3>Video performance</h3> \n        <div id=\"reviewImageComparisonWidget-16879797\" class=\"imageComparisonContainer\"></div> \n        <script type=\"text/javascript\">$(document).ready(function() { ImageComparisonWidget({\"containerId\":\"reviewImageComparisonWidget-16879797\",\"widgetId\":811,\"initialStateId\":null}) })</script> \n        <p>Video quality from the X-E4 is identical to that of its siblings, the X-S10 and X-T30; which is to say, quite good. <span class=\"linkish imageComparisonLink\" id=\"icl-5412-891980078\">Full HD footage</span><script type=\"text/javascript\">$(document).ready(function() { $(\"#icl-5412-891980078\").click(function() { ImageComparisonWidgetLink(5412); }); })</script> offers nice detail, though it is somewhat prone to moiré. <span class=\"linkish imageComparisonLink\" id=\"icl-5408--1512120132\">4K footage </span><script type=\"text/javascript\">$(document).ready(function() { $(\"#icl-5408--1512120132\").click(function() { ImageComparisonWidgetLink(5408); }); })</script> looks excellent – whether shooting UHD or DCI – offering significantly more detail than the <span class=\"linkish imageComparisonLink\" id=\"icl-5409-435580251\">Canon EOS M6 II</span><script type=\"text/javascript\">$(document).ready(function() { $(\"#icl-5409-435580251\").click(function() { ImageComparisonWidgetLink(5409); }); })</script>, a bit more detail than the <span class=\"linkish imageComparisonLink\" id=\"icl-5410-1577335602\">Nikon Z50</span><script type=\"text/javascript\">$(document).ready(function() { $(\"#icl-5410-1577335602\").click(function() { ImageComparisonWidgetLink(5410); }); })</script>, and similar amounts to <span class=\"linkish imageComparisonLink\" id=\"icl-5411-97269786\">Sony a6000-series</span><script type=\"text/javascript\">$(document).ready(function() { $(\"#icl-5411-97269786\").click(function() { ImageComparisonWidgetLink(5411); }); })</script> cameras.</p> \n        <p><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/reviews/fujifilm-x-e4-review-small-size-big-image-quality#top\"><strong>Back to top</strong></a></p> \n        <hr> \n         <h2 id=\"conclusion\" style=\"margin-top: 8%;\">Conclusion</h2> \n         <table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCaptions noCrop singleNoBorder center\" data-image-height=\"\" data-image-width=\"590\"> \n          <tbody> \n           <tr> \n            <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 590px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/0601644611/Product/Fujifilm-X-E4-Screen.jpeg\" target=\"article-0601644611\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"1180\" height=\"393\" src=\"https://3.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS1180x0~articles/0601644611/Product/Fujifilm-X-E4-Screen.jpeg\" width=\"590\" data-filename=\"Product/Fujifilm-X-E4-Screen.jpeg\" /></a></td> \n           </tr> \n          </tbody> \n         </table> \n         <div class=\"contentTable\"> \n          <table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"contentTable\"> \n           <tbody> \n            <tr> \n             <th width=\"50%\">What we like</th> \n             <th width=\"50%\">What we don't like</th> \n            </tr> \n            <tr> \n             <td width=\"50%\"> \n              <ul> \n               <li>Excellent image quality, pleasing JPEG color</li> \n               <li>Nice classic styling and compact design</li> \n               <li>Strong video feature set with good-quality Full HD and 4K video</li> \n               <li>The tilting touch screen is highly-responsive</li> \n               <li>Can use USB-C port for headphones with included dongle</li> \n               <li>In-camera charging</li> \n               <li>Good battery life</li> \n              </ul> </td> \n             <td width=\"50%\"> \n              <ul> \n               <li>Autofocus tracking performance lags behind the competition</li> \n               <li>No animal detection AF mode</li> \n               <li>We miss having a rear dial and focus mode selector (like on X-E3)</li> \n               <li>More custom buttons would be nice</li> \n               <li>The camera is slippery without accessory grip</li> \n               <li>No in-body stabilization</li> \n               <li>No weather-sealing</li> \n              </ul> </td> \n            </tr> \n           </tbody> \n          </table> \n         </div> \n         <p>Fujifilm has positioned the X-E4 as the <a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/reviews/fujifilm-x100v-review\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">X100V</a>'s twin with interchangeable lenses. But unlike previous generations of X-E and X100 cameras, this is not quite a fair positioning. The two share a lot of technology, but the X-E4 comes up a tad short next to its <a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/reviews/fujifilm-x100v-review/8\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">gold-award-winning</a> sibling in several regards. The most notable are a lack of weather-sealing, a lower-resolution EVF, and a paring down of control points that at best, leads to a more straightforward shooting experience, and at worst, an occasionally frustrating one.</p> \n         <blockquote class=\"pullQuote\">\n           We wish Fujifilm hadn't removed the front focus mode selector and rear dial found on its predecessor \n         </blockquote> \n         <p>The X-E4 does get a lot of things right, in terms of design. The 3\" tilting touchscreen is highly responsive and enjoyable to use, especially for street photography. And the 2.36M-dot EVF, while not jaw-dropping in resolution, should offer plenty of detail for most users. The camera is also quite handsome, not to mention compact, even if we found it rather slippery without its $90 accessory grip or $70 thumbrest. The paring down of control points left us frustrated, though. We wish Fujifilm hadn't removed the front focus mode selector and rear dial found on its <a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/reviews/fujifilm-x-e3-review\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">predecessor</a>. We also wish it had more than just three physical custom buttons.</p> \n         <table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCrop singleNoBorder center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"590\"> \n          <tbody> \n           <tr> \n            <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 590px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/0601644611/Samples/DSCF1194.acr.jpeg\" target=\"article-0601644611\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"1180\" height=\"393\" src=\"https://2.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS1180x0~articles/0601644611/Samples/DSCF1194.acr.jpeg\" width=\"590\" data-filename=\"Samples/DSCF1194.acr.jpeg\" /></a></td> \n           </tr> \n           <tr> \n            <td class=\"caption\" style=\"width: 590px;\"> <p>Converted from Raw in Adobe Camera Raw.</p> <p>ISO 160 |F2.8 | 1/450 sec | Tokina 23mm F1.4 <br><em>Photo: Dan Bracaglia</em></br></p> </td> \n           </tr> \n          </tbody> \n         </table> \n         <p>In terms of image quality output, the X-E4 is highly capable, thanks to its excellent pedigree. Image quality is a match for the <a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/reviews/fujifilm-x-t4-review\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">flagship X-T4</a>. Fujifilm's latest X-Trans BSI CMOS 4 sensor is capable of excellent Raw files with good detail capture and lots of editing latitude. And Fujifilm JPEG profiles – which mimic classic film stocks – have long been a DPR staff favorite. The X-E4 offers a whopping 18, including 'Classic Chrome,' 'Classic Negative' and 'Acros' (to name some favorites).</p> \n         <blockquote class=\"pullQuote\">\n           The only important video-centric feature absent from the X-E4 is in-body image stabilization for hand-held shooting \n         </blockquote> \n         <p>Video-wise, the X-E4 is also highly capable with nicely detailed 4K output, including 8-bit Log capture internally and 10-bit Log capture to a dedicated capture device (via Micro-HDMI). Full HD video can be captured at up 240 fps, for all your super-slow motion needs. And you can plug in a microphone and headphones (the latter via USB-C to audio dongle). Arguably, the only important video-centric feature absent from the X-E4 is in-body image stabilization for hand-held shooting.</p> \n         <table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCrop singleNoBorder center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"590\"> \n          <tbody> \n           <tr> \n            <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 590px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/0601644611/Samples/DSCF1098.jpeg\" target=\"article-0601644611\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"1180\" height=\"393\" src=\"https://1.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS1180x0~articles/0601644611/Samples/DSCF1098.jpeg\" width=\"590\" data-filename=\"Samples/DSCF1098.jpeg\" /></a></td> \n           </tr> \n           <tr> \n            <td class=\"caption\" style=\"width: 590px;\"> <p>Out-of-camera JPEG shot using the 'Astia/Soft' film simulation.</p> <p>ISO 160 | F2.8 |1/220 sec | Tokina 23mm F1.4<br><em>Photo: Dan Bracaglia</em></br></p> </td> \n           </tr> \n          </tbody> \n         </table> \n         <p>One notable area Fujifilm cameras tend to lag behind their closest competitors is autofocus subject tracking performance, and the X-E4 is no exception. For mostly static subjects, face and eye detection work well enough, as does the traditional subject tracking AF mode. But once you introduce movement, these modes become much less reliable. That said, AF performance using a single point or zone in AF-C works very well and the AF joystick is highly responsive.</p> \n         <blockquote class=\"pullQuote\">\n           We suspect the X-E4 is going to make a lot of photographers happy, especially those craving a near-pocket-size X-mount body with Fujifilm's latest IQ performance \n         </blockquote> \n         <p>Ultimately, the X-E4 is a camera with a lot to offer and we suspect it is going to make a lot of photographers happy, especially those craving a near-pocket-size X-mount body with Fujifilm's latest IQ performance. For those upgrading from other Fujifilm bodies, the lack of buttons will likely take some getting used to, but don't let that be a deal-breaker. This is a camera anyone on staff at DPReview would be happy to grab for an afternoon of street photography or take on a long vacation – once that's a thing again.</p> \n         <h3>Compared to its peers</h3> \n         <table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCaptions noCrop singleNoBorder center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"590\"> \n          <tbody> \n           <tr> \n            <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 590px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/0601644611/Product/Fujifilm-X-E4-lead-03.jpeg\" target=\"article-0601644611\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"1180\" height=\"393\" src=\"https://3.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS1180x0~articles/0601644611/Product/Fujifilm-X-E4-lead-03.jpeg\" width=\"590\" data-filename=\"Product/Fujifilm-X-E4-lead-03.jpeg\" /></a></td> \n           </tr> \n          </tbody> \n         </table> \n         <p>The X-E4's nearest competitor is the <a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/reviews/sony-a6400-review\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\"><strong>Sony a6400</strong></a>, a camera with very similar specs but offering a very different shooting experience: Where the X-E4 is more hands-on, the a6400 encourages a more set-it-and-forget-it mindset. Both cameras are rangefinder-style in design, and while we prefer the touchscreen and control points of the X-E4, we find the autofocus system of the a6400 far more capable. Both cameras offer good image and video quality, and you'll get great Raw files from both, but we find Fujifilm's JPEGs more pleasing.</p> \n         <p>Another competitor with similar specs is the SLR-style <strong><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/reviews/nikon-z50-review\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">Nikon Z50</a></strong>. Both it and the X-E4 are well-rounded cameras offering plenty of capability. We prefer the Nikon's ergonomics and control points, but appreciate Fujifilm's considerably larger family of native APS-C lenses. You'll get a bit more resolution from the X-E4, but not an earth-shattering amount, along with slightly more detailed 4K. But your choice between these two may ultimately come down to preference between SLR- or rangefinder-style.</p> \n         <p>The <a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/reviews/canon-eos-m6-ii-review\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\"><strong>Canon EOS M6 Mark II</strong></a> is also a natural competitor to the X-E4, sporting similar specs. The most notable difference: the Canon doesn't have a built-in EVF, but it does offer an accessory unit for the hotshoe making it more expensive. Both are highly capable in the image quality department, though the Canon does offer more resolution. But on the video side, we much prefer the X-E4's output and feature set. We think the Fufjilm is a better looking camera than the Canon, but appreciate that latter's hardy grip and ample control points. But there's a lot more native glass available for the X-E4 than the M6 II, and the X-E4 offers superior battery life.</p> \n         <p>The<a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/reviews/fujifilm-x-s10-review\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\"><strong> Fujfiilm X-S10</strong></a> is also a sensible competitor to the X-E4. It's essentially the same camera under the hood, but in an SLR-shaped body with a deeper, more comfortable grip, better controls, and in-body image stabilization. All that comes with a slightly higher price tag, though.</p> \n         <p><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/reviews/fujifilm-x-e4-review-small-size-big-image-quality#top\"><strong>Back to top</strong></a></p> \n         <hr> \n          <h2 id=\"samples\" style=\"margin-top: 8%;\">Sample gallery</h2> \n          <p>Please do not reproduce any of these images without prior permission \n              </tr> \n              <tr class=\"summary\"> \n               <td colspan=\"2\"> \n                <div class=\"conclusion\">\n                  Conclusion \n                </div> \n                <div class=\"summary\">\n                  The X-E4 is a stylish camera capable of excellent image quality and packed with useful features. It's the brand's smallest X-mount offering and a good choice for street, travel, and generalist photographers. It's also capable of strong video performance, though there's no in-body stabilization for hand-held shooting. The only thing the X-E4 doesn't excel at is AF tracking; you'll find quite a few of its competitors offer better tracking and face/eye detection. \n                </div></td> \n              </tr> \n              <tr class=\"goodForNotSoGoodFor\"> \n               <td colspan=\"2\"> \n                <table cellspacing=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" border=\"0\"> \n                 <tr> \n                  <td> \n                   <table cellspacing=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" border=\"0\"> \n                    <tr class=\"suitability goodFor\"> \n                     <td><span class=\"circleBackground\"></span> \n                      <div class=\"label\">\n                        Good for \n                      </div> \n                      <div class=\"text\">\n                        Generalists looking for a capable and compact interchangeable lens camera. Street and travel photographers. Those wishing to shoot JPEGs only. \n                      </div></td> \n                    </tr> \n                   </table></td> \n                  <td> \n                   <table cellspacing=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" border=\"0\"> \n                    <tr class=\"suitability notGoodFor\"> \n                     <td><span class=\"circleBackground\"></span> \n                      <div class=\"label\">\n                        Not so good for \n                      </div> \n                      <div class=\"text\">\n                        Sports and action shooters needing the best AF performance. Video shooters needing in-body stabilization. \n                      </div></td> \n                    </tr> \n                   </table></td> \n                 </tr> \n Texas-based photographer <a href=\"https://www.instagram.com/mir_or_image/\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">Mir-or-Image </a>believes they can. In his ongoing video series, '<a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/playlist?list=PLtPGdFzLX1a5JwqbYpSsKbTDPqev_M_AD\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">Photo Mode Perspective</a>,' Mir plays popular video games and uses their built-in photo modes to help viewers learn the basics of photography, including principles of composition, how shutter speed and aperture impact the look and feel of an image, and more. Mir loves video games and photography. With his educational video series, he combines these two passions in a distinct and educational way.</p> \n<p>Photo modes in video games have become increasingly more sophisticated. For example, in the PlayStation 4 game 'God of War,' the included photo mode includes sliders for the field of view and focal length, which are, of course, interconnected. As you increase the field of view, the focal length decreases. This is something that experienced photographers take for granted, but for beginners, understanding how focal length changes perspective in a scene is important.</p> \n<p>Likewise, for seasoned shooters, you understand how aperture changes the depth of field, all else equal. Still, the photo mode in 'God of War' and other games offers a helpful visual representation of how the plane of focus changes with aperture. Put in simple terms, 'Here's something to note with f-stop, the smaller the number, the blurrier the background gets,' Mir says in the video below. Using 'God of War,' Mir also discusses ways to crop images and edit brightness, contrast and colors, and more.</p> \n<div class=\"video\">\n <iframe allowfullscreen=\"\" frameborder=\"0\" height=\"326\" id=\"videoFrame\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/CvMZxVjkp0g?rel=0&amp;autohide=1&amp;wmode=transparent&amp;enablejsapi=1\" width=\"580\"></iframe>\n</div> \n<p>Another PlayStation game with a very capable built-in photo mode is 2020's 'Ghost of Tsushima.' The game, developed by Sucker Punch Productions, is set on Japan's Tsushima island during the first Mongol invasion of Japan. Some creative liberties are taken in the game for narrative and gameplay purposes, but it nonetheless provides a stunning backdrop for taking in-game photos.</p> \n<p>Like 'God of War,' 'Ghost of Tsushima' includes focal length and aperture sliders for your virtual lens. If you want to shoot a portrait of the main character, Jin, you can use a virtual 85mm f/1.8 lens, for example. You can even direct your subject, in a sense, by changing the character's pose and facial expression. To add creative flair, you can adjust exposure compensation (bias), add particle effects, change the lighting, color grade your image and more. Also, as a warning, 'Ghost of Tsushima' is a violent video game and there is some virtual blood in the video below.</p> \n<div class=\"video\">\n <iframe allowfullscreen=\"\" frameborder=\"0\" height=\"326\" id=\"videoFrame\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/hAbNBbQlCSU?rel=0&amp;autohide=1&amp;wmode=transparent&amp;enablejsapi=1\" width=\"580\"></iframe>\n</div> \n<p>Over at <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCmJZXtZIXw2EDPWhyUO2cpg\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">Mir's YouTube channel</a> you can also see his 'Photo Mode Perspective' videos for two more video games, 'Cyberpunk 2077' and 'Spider-Man: Miles Morales.' To view Mir's real-world photography, follow him on <a href=\"https://www.instagram.com/mir_or_image/\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">Instagram</a> and visit his <a href=\"https://www.mir-or-image.com/home\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">website</a>. The photography bug bit Mir during a trip to Europe in 2018. He enjoyed using his smartphone in manual mode, and when he returned home to Texas, he went out and bought an interchangeable lens camera. He is now a professional car photographer based in Houston.</p> \n<table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCrop singleNoBorder center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"590\"> \n <tbody> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 590px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/1633276520/forza-horizon-4-image.jpeg\" target=\"article-620e6d19e21840849d36eeeab8ec6f38\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"590\" height=\"330\" src=\"https://4.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS590x0~articles/1633276520/forza-horizon-4-image.jpeg\" width=\"590\" data-filename=\"forza-horizon-4-image.jpeg\" /></a></td> \n  </tr> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"caption\" style=\"width: 590px;\">I captured this image in 'Forza Horizon 4' on Xbox. It's exceedingly unlikely that I'll ever have the chance to photograph a 1962 Ferrari 250 GTO in the Scottish highlands in real life, so it's neat that I get to photography rare cars in different locations in a racing video game.</td> \n  </tr> \n </tbody> \n</table> \n<p>Videogames can do more than help aspiring photographers learn more about how camera and lens settings impact the photos they capture. For example, professional automotive photographer Sam Dobbins <a href=\"https://altdriver.com/gaming/video-professional-car-photographer-used-forza-game-to-plan-magazine-photoshoot/\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">used Forza Motorsport on Xbox to plan out a real-world photoshoot</a>. Others, such as Instagram user <a href=\"https://www.instagram.com/jk_fh4_pics/\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">jk_fh4_pics</a> has an entire account dedicated to photography from the game 'Forza Horizon 4.' In some cases, game developers even hold photography contests using their games, which is something that Playground Games does with Forza Horizon and Rockstar Games does with Red Dead Redemption 2.</p> \n<div class=\"video\">\n <iframe allowfullscreen=\"\" frameborder=\"0\" height=\"326\" id=\"videoFrame\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/e-e-lev6iiA?rel=0&amp;autohide=1&amp;wmode=transparent&amp;enablejsapi=1\" width=\"580\"></iframe>\n</div> \n<p>If you're like Mir and love both video games and photography, you may be able to combine your interests like him. 'New Pokémon Snap' arrives on Nintendo Switch later this month, and the entire purpose of that game is to capture photos of Pokémon in their virtual habitats.</p> \n<p>The upcoming Switch title will allow Pokémon shutterbugs to edit and share their images online with other gamers. A similar game is a PlayStation 3 title from 2008, 'Afrika,' in which the player assumes the role of a photojournalist hired to take photos on an African safari. It's a difficult game to find these days, but I remember importing a copy from Japan when I became interested in photography in high school. Canon’s statement came in the form of its <a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/news/7035809882/canon-annual-financial-results-show-drop-net-sales-increase-profits-point-positive-2021\">full-year 2020 financial results presentation</a>, while Sigma’s statement came directly from Sigma CEO Kazuto Yamaki, who said in a <a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/news/5000050197/sigma-ceo-confirms-rf-z-mount-possibility-estimates-camera-industry-stabilize/1\">recent interview</a> that he expects the camera market ‘will reach its minimal size [in 2020]’ and be ‘pretty stable’ going forward.</p> \n<p>While this might’ve been difficult to imagine, especially after the impact COVID-19 had on the global economy throughout 2020, it seems the predictions are holding true, so far. Based on CIPA data, which tracks the global production and shipment of camera models from <a href=\"https://www.cipa.jp/stats/documents/e/list_e.pdf\">these camera manufacturers</a>, production and shipment numbers are tracking the best it’s been since 2017.</p> \n<table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCrop singleNoBorder center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"590\"> \n <tbody> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 590px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/8487085806/10E50C2D-B6F3-4B84-8D1D-57562C74FCDD.jpeg\" target=\"article-a45c525d03d046e38d99e49de34ce507\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"590\" height=\"437\" src=\"https://2.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS590x0~articles/8487085806/10E50C2D-B6F3-4B84-8D1D-57562C74FCDD.jpeg\" width=\"590\" data-filename=\"10E50C2D-B6F3-4B84-8D1D-57562C74FCDD.jpeg\" /></a></td> \n  </tr> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"caption\" style=\"width: 590px;\">This chart from CIPA shows total digital stills camera shipments in 2019 (purple, circles), 2020 (black, triangles) and 2021 (orange, squares). These numbers include compact cameras with built-in lenses, DSLR cameras and mirrorless cameras. Click to enlarge.</td> \n  </tr> \n </tbody> \n</table> \n<p>Specifically, CIPA’s data shows total digital still camera shipments were down 12.7% by volume and up 9% by value compared to the same timeframe last year (January and February)—and that’s averaged out with the shipment numbers of compact cameras with built-in lenses. If you look at the data for interchangeable lens cameras, shipments are down just 6.2% by volume and up 17.3% by value, year-over-year (YoY) for January and February.</p> \n<table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCrop singleNoBorder center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"590\"> \n <tbody> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 590px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/8487085806/063C14A5-7AFA-4037-876A-F93E18CE6279.jpeg\" target=\"article-a45c525d03d046e38d99e49de34ce507\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"590\" height=\"438\" src=\"https://4.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS590x0~articles/8487085806/063C14A5-7AFA-4037-876A-F93E18CE6279.jpeg\" width=\"590\" data-filename=\"063C14A5-7AFA-4037-876A-F93E18CE6279.jpeg\" /></a></td> \n  </tr> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"caption\" style=\"width: 590px;\">This chart from CIPA shows total interchangeable lens shipments in 2019 (purple, circles), 2020 (black, triangles) and 2021 (orange, squares).</td> \n  </tr> \n </tbody> \n</table> \n<p>Break that number down even further and you’ll see that, much like compact cameras shipments are affecting the total digital camera market, DSLR cameras are dragging down the average for interchangeable lens cameras. If you isolate mirrorless interchangeable lens cameras, shipments YoY for January and February are up 3.2% by volume and up an impressive 44.5% by value.</p> \n<table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCrop singleNoBorder center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"590\"> \n <tbody> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 590px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/8487085806/353D1537-ED6A-4035-A603-144383A5C945.jpeg\" target=\"article-a45c525d03d046e38d99e49de34ce507\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"590\" height=\"392\" src=\"https://3.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS590x0~articles/8487085806/353D1537-ED6A-4035-A603-144383A5C945.jpeg\" width=\"590\" data-filename=\"353D1537-ED6A-4035-A603-144383A5C945.jpeg\" /></a></td> \n  </tr> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"caption\" style=\"width: 590px;\">CIPA’s complete breakdown, which shows production and shipment data from January and February 2021 by camera type and region. Click to enlarge.</td> \n  </tr> \n </tbody> \n</table> \n<p>These numbers don’t paint the entire picture, as this is only taking into account production and shipments—not sales. Still though, the YoY numbers are some of the best we’ve seen in a while from CIPA and the data backs up what some of the major camera companies have emphasized over the past years in their interviews and financial result presentations for investors; the camera market is beginning to stabilize as the drop-off at the lower end of the market has more or less reached a plateau and hobbyist and professional photographers—who are less likely to trade out their dedicated cameras for smartphones—are starting to once again make up the majority of the market.</p> \n<p>Considering March 2020 is when the COVID-19 pandemic really started to impact the global economy, contextualizing the rest of CIPA’s 2021 data will prove to be more difficult. Specifically, we’re going to see high YoY numbers for both production and shipments, due to both being limited in 2020 due to the COVID-19 pandemic, but in future reports we’ll do our best to contextualize CIPA’s data to ensure we have a solid macro-level view of the photography market.</p> \n<p>You can view CIPA’s February data (and all historical data) on <a +0000","feedId":70,"bgimg":"https://4.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS590x0~articles/8487085806/FA5B3722-6EF9-4FBC-B7B9-C1A9A4610496.jpeg","linkMd5":"9ea03b800a420fbc2356046384137c83","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn46@2020_3/2021/04/07/17-38-14-321_16c758d370647024.webp","destWidth":590,"destHeight":393,"sourceBytes":71691,"destBytes":36552,"author":"","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://4.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS590x0~articles/8487085806/FA5B3722-6EF9-4FBC-B7B9-C1A9A4610496.jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn46@2020_3/2021/04/07/17-38-14-321_16c758d370647024.webp","https://2.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS590x0~articles/8487085806/10E50C2D-B6F3-4B84-8D1D-57562C74FCDD.jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn34@2020_3/2021/04/07/17-38-31-842_fc01cf61aee22274.webp","https://4.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS590x0~articles/8487085806/063C14A5-7AFA-4037-876A-F93E18CE6279.jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx19/cdn11@2020_1/2021/04/07/17-38-44-629_cde64fcde1493d16.webp","https://3.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS590x0~articles/8487085806/353D1537-ED6A-4035-A603-144383A5C945.jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn20@2020_1/2021/04/07/17-38-32-703_872cdf0a167d8662.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1617817093449},{"createdTime":"2021-04-08 01:38:13","updatedTime":"2021-04-08 01:38:13","title":"Hubble scientists revisit an incredible image of Veil Nebula, showing off new details","link":"https://www.dpreview.com/news/5134615536/hubble-scientists-revisit-an-incredible-image-of-veil-nebula-showing-off-new-details","description":"<table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCaptions noCrop singleNoBorder center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"590\"> \n <tbody> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 590px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/5134615536/hs-2021-veil-nebula-banner.jpeg\" target=\"article-5134615536\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"590\" height=\"442\" src=\"https://2.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS590x0~articles/5134615536/hs-2021-veil-nebula-banner.jpeg\" width=\"590\" data-filename=\"hs-2021-veil-nebula-banner.jpeg\" /></a></td> \n  </tr> \n </tbody> \n</table> \n<p>In 2015, the <a href=\"https://www.nasa.gov/mission_pages/hubble/main/index.html\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">Hubble Space Telescope</a> captured an <a href=\"https://www.nasa.gov/image-feature/veil-nebula-supernova-remnant\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">image</a> of the Veil Nebula. NASA has <a href=\"https://www.nasa.gov/image-feature/goddard/2021/hubble-revisits-the-veil-nebula\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">revisited</a> this image and applied new processing techniques, bringing out even finer details of the nebula.</p> \n<p>NASA, ESA/Hubble and Z. Levay have been able to bring out additional details in the ionized gas that makes up the threads and filaments of the nebula. Observations taken by Hubble's Wide Field Camera 3 instrument using five different filters were combined with new post-processing methods to create the new image. You can see enhanced details of emissions from doubly ionized oxygen (seen in the image as blue colors), ionized hydrogen, ionized sulfur (green) and ionized nitrogen (seen as reds in the photo).</p> \n<table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCrop singleNoBorder center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"590\"> \n <tbody> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 590px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/5134615536/hs-2021-veil-nebula.jpeg\" target=\"article-d69170a007c5413db223f7a52c152cc0\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"590\" height=\"413\" src=\"https://3.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS590x0~articles/5134615536/hs-2021-veil-nebula.jpeg\" width=\"590\" data-filename=\"hs-2021-veil-nebula.jpeg\" /></a></td> \n  </tr> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"caption\" style=\"width: 590px;\">This close-up <a href=\"https://www.nasa.gov/sites/default/files/thumbnails/image/potw2113a.jpg\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">image</a> of the Veil Nebula was first captured in 2015. It has been reprocessed to show a better view of the nebula and its filaments of ionized gas. The ionized gas is all that remains of a supernova that about 20 times the mass of the Sun. 'The fast-moving blast wave from the ancient explosion is plowing into a wall of cool, denser interstellar gas, emitting light. The nebula lies along the edge of a large bubble of low-density gas that was blown into space by the dying star prior to its self-detonation.' Image credit: ESA/Hubble &amp; NASA, Z. Levay</td> \n  </tr> \n </tbody> \n</table> \n<p>The Veil Nebula is about 2,100 light-years from Earth in the constellation of Cygnus, otherwise known as the 'Swan.' As NASA <a href=\"https://www.nasa.gov/image-feature/goddard/2021/hubble-revisits-the-veil-nebula\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">writes</a>, in astronomical terms, Cygnus is a relatively close neighbor.</p> \n<table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCrop singleNoBorder center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"590\"> \n <tbody> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 590px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/5134615536/hs-2021-veil-nebula-closeup.jpeg\" target=\"article-d69170a007c5413db223f7a52c152cc0\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"590\" height=\"590\" src=\"https://3.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS590x0~articles/5134615536/hs-2021-veil-nebula-closeup.jpeg\" width=\"590\" data-filename=\"hs-2021-veil-nebula-closeup.jpeg\" /></a></td> \n  </tr> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"caption\" style=\"width: 590px;\">100% crop of the above image. To download the massive image for yourself, <a href=\"https://www.nasa.gov/sites/default/files/thumbnails/image/potw2113a.jpg\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">click here</a>.</td> \n  </tr> \n </tbody> \n</table> \n<p>Astronomer William Herschel first identified the Veil Nebula way back in 1784. In 1904, Herschel's work was followed by Williamina Fleming's discovery of a fainter portion of the nebula, known as Pickering's Triangle, named after the director of the Harvard College Observatory where Fleming worked. If you'd like to view the Veil Nebula for yourself, the best observation time is early autumn in the northern hemisphere and early spring in the southern hemisphere. The nebula is not visible to the naked eye, but it can be seen through a telescope or binoculars under dark sky conditions. If you have a nebula filter, it will help brighten the Veil's appearance and allow you to see additional detail.</p> \n<p>The Veil Nebula is a visible portion of the Cygnus Loop, which is the remnant of a supernova formed about 10,000 years ago. The Veil Nebula formed through the death of a massive star, which possessed roughly 20 times the mass of the Sun. Like other stars of that size, it had a relatively short lifespan and died with a massive release of energy. The energy and debris from this supernova form the Veil Nebula's tendrils of ionized gas.</p> \n<table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" class=\"images noCrop singleNoBorder center\" data-image-height=\"null\" data-image-width=\"590\"> \n <tbody> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"image\" style=\"width: 590px;\"><a href=\"https://www.dpreview.com/files/p/articles/5134615536/hs-2015-29-veil-nebula.jpeg\" target=\"article-d69170a007c5413db223f7a52c152cc0\"><img border=\"0\" data-thumbnail-height=\"0\" data-thumbnail-width=\"590\" height=\"393\" src=\"https://2.img-dpreview.com/files/p/E~TS590x0~articles/5134615536/hs-2015-29-veil-nebula.jpeg\" width=\"590\" data-filename=\"hs-2015-29-veil-nebula.jpeg\" /></a></td> \n  </tr> \n  <tr> \n   <td class=\"caption\" style=\"width: 590px;\">The 2015 version of the image of the Veil Nebula. Image credit: NASA/ESA/Hubble Heritage Team</td> \n  </tr> \n </tbody> \n</table> \n<p>The original image and the reprocessed version show only a small section of the Veil Nebula, which is continually expanding. The entire nebula is 110 light-years across, covering about six full moons' worth of the night sky as viewed from Earth. The section we see in the shot from Hubble, which is a six-image composite, is about two light-years across.</p> \n<p>Back in 2015, when showing off its new image of the Veil Nebula, NASA also shared a couple of neat videos. The videos haven't been redone with the latest processed image, but they're nonetheless worth checking out again.</p> \n<div class=\"video\"> \n <iframe allowfullscreen=\"\" frameborder=\"0\" height=\"326\" id=\"videoFrame\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/27PErpOJ7VA?rel=0&amp;autohide=1&amp;wmode=transparent&amp;enablejsapi=1\" width=\"580\"></iframe> \n</div> \n<div class=\"video\"> \n <iframe allowfullscreen=\"\" frameborder=\"0\" height=\"326\" id=\"videoFrame\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/rsqZlXREz2E?rel=0&amp;autohide=1&amp;wmode=transparent&amp;enablejsapi=1\" width=\"580\"></iframe> \n</div> \n<p>You can learn more about the Veil Nebula by <a href=\"https://www.nasa.gov/feature/goddard/caldwell-34\" rel=\"noopener\" target=\"_blank\">visiting Hubble's Caldwell catalog</a>.
